# Brock Rumlow — UATU INTELLIGENCE DOSSIER

*Full-existence intelligence briefing. Independent, evidence-based assessment — the benevolent inverse of total surveillance.*


## Executive Brief (BLUF)

# EXECUTIVE BRIEF — BLUF

**Subject:** Brock Rumlow. Operational aliases: *Crossbones* (primary, post-1990), *Bender*, *Brixton Rumlow* (peripheral); Frank Simpson designation disambiguated and excluded. Date of file: current through Secret Empire epoch and ancillary subsequent appearances. Reviewer: UATU, behavioral reconstruction cell.

---

## BOTTOM LINE UP FRONT

Rumlow is a **fully consolidated, organized sadistic antisocial personality** who, in late adolescence, was captured by an authoritarian organizing object (the Red Skull) and has spent the entirety of his adult life — roughly two and a half decades of operational record — discharging a constitutional appetite for cruelty inside the disciplinary scaffold that object provides. He is not a man with a dark side. He is a man whose interior, exterior, vocation, leisure, sexuality, aesthetics, and relational vocabulary have all been routed through a single channel: predation in service of a fascist patron. He is not in conflict with himself. He has not been in conflict with himself, on the evidence, since he was approximately fourteen years old. **This is the central fact of the file, and every operational recommendation flows from it.**

He is, in the precise clinical sense, **uncomplicated** — not simple-minded (he is operationally intelligent and capable of multi-stage strategic planning), but unconflicted. The interior architecture is integrated around its pathology rather than fractured by it. This makes him categorically distinct from the rogues' gallery taxon he is usually filed beside: he is not a Bullseye (chaotic, parasitic, Factor-2-heavy), not a Zemo (ideologue-aristocrat with succession ambition), not a Crossfire or a Taskmaster (pure mercenary, no ideological capture), and not a Bucky-template (an asset whose programming the self underneath resists). He is the rarer specimen — the antisocial who *found his cause*, integrated it, and never looked back.

---

## THE THROUGH-LINE

A single sentence captures the arc of his entire published existence: **he serves the Skull-line.** Every other biographical fact — every operation, every relationship, every disfigurement, every "death," every brief detour through Pleasant Hill or the Hydra-Cap apparatus — is subordinate to that one structural commitment.

Trace it across the eras and the through-line becomes unmistakable:

- **Adolescence (Lower East Side, Savage Crims):** the temperament is already complete. Group sexual assault, multiple homicides, the murder of an avenger's sister, an immediate pragmatic exile abroad. No remorse signature, no decompensation, no trauma response. He is *already the man who did it*. What is missing at this stage is not the predator but the discipline; he is feral, gifted, ungoverned.
- **Early twenties (Taskmaster's academy, then Red Skull recruitment):** the discipline arrives. Within a handful of years he is good enough at killing to *teach* professional killers. The Skull then acquires him — and this is the load-bearing event of the biography. The Skull supplies what the gang ecology could not: an ideological frame that elevates the predation from delinquency to *vocation*. From this moment forward, Rumlow is not a thug. He is a *consecrated instrument*.
- **The Gruenwald decade:** the consecrated instrument in operation. Diamondback's captivity arc reveals that his relational dialect outside the chain of command is the same dialect he uses inside it — possession, coercion, ownership. There is no "private Brock" who differs from the operational Crossbones. The man at work and the man off-duty are continuous.
- **The Brubaker years:** the maturation. He plans and executes the assassination of Steve Rogers on the courthouse steps. He partners with Sin in a coupling that fuses violence and sex without seam. He is disfigured by the Skull's reanimated body — and notably, *the Skull's body causing the injury does not interrupt the loyalty by a single panel*. He is then made permanent inside the mask.
- **Fear Itself and after:** Sin becomes Skadi. He transfers devotion downstream along the Skull-line with no friction. The object of loyalty is revealed to be not the man but the *line* — the project, the bloodline, the ideological succession.
- **Secret Empire epoch:** the deepest proof. He recognizes a Steve Rogers reframed as Hydra's prophet and serves *him* without contradiction, because what Rumlow tracks is not the face of the leader but the *signature of the project*. Hydra-Cap is the Skull's project. The loyalty migrates without internal protest.

**The through-line in one formulation:** a constitutional predator was captured early by a project worthy of his appetite, and he has spent his life as that project's most reliable distal limb. He has never seriously considered another life. He has never auditioned another self. He has never, on the documentary record, paused.

---

## THE "WOUND" QUESTION — AND WHY THE USUAL FRAME FAILS

Standard intelligence-psychological doctrine assumes a **core wound** beneath an operational persona, and assumes that excavating or pressing that wound creates leverage. **This doctrine does not apply to Rumlow, and applying it will burn assets.**

There is no recoverable pre-pathological self. The earliest data we have on him already shows the finished temperament — sadism, predation, possession-coded relating, regulated affect under violence, absence of empathic resonance. We have no childhood. We have no protective figure to invoke. We have no "before the gang." The man we meet at fourteen, raping and killing in a Lower East Side basement, is the same man we meet at forty-five behind the skull mask. Continuity is the diagnostic finding.

What looks like a wound — and what less rigorous analysts have mis-coded as one — is in fact the *organizing structure*. The disfigurement, for instance: in a normal subject, full-thickness facial burns and permanent disfigurement produce body-image collapse, depressive sequelae, social withdrawal, and a documented mourning of the prior self. In Rumlow, the disfigurement produces **role consolidation** — operational tempo increases, the mask becomes face, the Crossbones identity overwrites the residual Brock-Rumlow identity, and the man becomes *more* of what he already was. This is not denial. Denial requires conflict. There is no conflict.

If a wound must be named to satisfy the template, it is this: **he has no second narrative**. He cannot tell himself any story about himself other than the one he is currently inside. The interior is a single room with no doors. This is not painful to him; he does not experience it as a wound. But it is, structurally, his only vulnerability — see below.

The wound, then, is the *absence of an alternative interior*. Its maintenance is automatic: every act of service to the Skull-line reinforces the only story he has; every act of cruelty discharges the appetite that would otherwise have nowhere to go; every morning behind the mask removes the question of who he might otherwise be. **The maintenance regimen is his life.** He does not need to repress, sublimate, or rationalize. He simply continues.

---

## WHO HE IS, AT THE DEEPEST LEVEL

Stripping away the operational surface and the persona apparatus:

He is an **organized predator** for whom cruelty is the primary reward channel, dominance is the only legible mode of relating, and an authoritarian object is the only available form of love. He has the discipline of a senior NCO, the patience of a sniper, the appetites of a serial sexual offender, and the ideological credulity of a true believer who has skipped the philosophy and absorbed only the conclusions. He is, behaviorally, what a fascist movement produces when it gets exactly the kind of subordinate it most wants: not the chaotic brownshirt but the *competent enforcer who never asks*.

The most underrated fact about him is his **discipline**. He does not drink to excess. He does not narcotize. He does not parasitically exploit the organization that employs him. He does not chase rank above his station. He trains, executes, reports, and waits. This is what makes him a strategic asset rather than a tactical hazard, and it is what should most concern any agency mapping him. The dangerous Crossbones is not the snarling one in the panel; it is the patient one outside the panel, who has been in position for six hours and will be in position for six more.

The second most underrated fact is the **purity of the vertical orientation**. He has no peers. Sin is partner-coded but is also Skull-line; she is loved *as succession*, not as equal. Subordinates exist to be commanded and, where useful, terrified. Enemies exist to be killed theatrically enough to mean something to them before they die. *There is no lateral relational capacity in his record.* This is not loneliness — loneliness requires the recognition of absence — but it is a structural fact that bears on every prediction about his behavior under stress.

The third underrated fact is the **fusion of sex and violence** as paired stimuli. The Diamondback captivity and the Sin partnership are the same psychic mechanism viewed through two windows. He cannot conceive of intimacy that is not predation, and he cannot conceive of predation that is not, at some register, intimate. This makes him predictable in the presence of certain stimuli and makes his sexual conduct an extension of his operational conduct rather than a separate domain.

---

## THE OPERATIONAL SUMMARY

**Threat envelope.** Persistent. High-end enhanced human, peak unenhanced baseline with intermittent serum augmentation; expert in firearms, demolitions, edged weapons, and hand-to-hand at a tier capable of instructing professional killers. Comfortable across solo wetwork, small-team command, and large-formation tactical leadership. Operationally patient. Strategically planful. Personally fearless to a degree that is not bravado but constitutional — the affect that would produce fear is largely absent.

**Predictability.** High, once the organizing object is identified. He goes where the Skull-line goes. He kills what the Skull-line designates. His personal vendettas (Diamondback, Rogers, Barnes) are real but subordinate; he will defer them when the project requires deferral. This makes him *mappable* in a way more chaotic operators are not.

**Non-leverage points (do not pursue).** Remorse appeals. Childhood-trauma framing. Body-image / disfigurement humiliation as standalone tactic. Substance-use leverage. Lateral relational appeals ("you have friends," "you are loved"). Ideological argumentation on the merits. None of these have purchase on the structure described.

**Leverage points (in descending order of analytic confidence):**

1. **Displacement or corruption of the organizing object.** The single highest-yield vector. Convincing him that the Skull-line has *used and discarded* him — not betrayed him in a romantic sense, but disposed of him as instrument — produces a category of identity vertigo he has no fallback narrative to absorb. He will not become good. He will become unmoored, and an unmoored Rumlow is briefly less effective than an integrated one, which is the operational window.
2. **Substitution within the enforcer slot.** His grandiosity is invested in being *the* right hand. Demonstrating, visibly and to the Skull-line, a preferred replacement enforcer wounds him where physical injury does not. Use only in coordination with (1); standalone it merely produces a rage spike and degrades his patience without dislodging the structure.
3. **Diamondback as destabilizer.** The single unfinished possession in his record. Her presence, image, or voice, deployed at operational moments, reliably reroutes attention from mission to grudge. Tactically exploitable; ethically constrained.
4. **Forced unmasking before the Skull-line or subordinates.** A narrow, situational tool. The face under the mask is not, to him, an object of private grief, but its exposure to the hierarchy he serves produces a humiliation response his outward-facing defenses cannot metabolize.

**What will not happen, on any reasonable timeline.** Redemption. Reform. Defection on conscience. The "shown the light" arc. A romantic reorientation toward a non-predatory partner. A quiet retirement. Therapeutic engagement of any productive kind. These outcomes are not improbable in his case; they are structurally precluded by the architecture described.

**What will happen, repeatedly.** Return. He has been killed and returned multiple times across the published record, and even setting aside the metaphysical mechanics, the *behavioral* return is the relevant pattern: presented with an opening, he resumes. There is no internal exhaustion. The appetite does not fatigue. The discipline does not erode. As long as a Skull-line project exists for him to serve, he will serve it, and when one does not exist he will wait for one with a patience that civilian observers consistently underestimate.

---

## CLOSING ANALYTIC STATEMENT

Most subjects in a file of this depth disclose, somewhere in the longitudinal record, a moment of self-division — a hesitation, a confession, a relationship that did not fit the pattern, a private practice that contradicted the public role. Such moments are the analyst's purchase. **Rumlow does not provide one.** Across thirty-five years of documented behavior, four major authorial regimes, and every imaginable operational and personal pressure — including disfigurement, imprisonment, the death of his patron, the succession of that patron's daughter, the unmasking of his enemies' weaknesses, and his own repeated mortality — the structure does not crack, does not flex, and does not disclose an alternative interior beneath itself.

The dossier on Rumlow is therefore not the usual document. It is not a map of a man's contradictions; it is a map of a man's *consistencies*. He is the rare subject whose surface is his depth. Plan against him accordingly: not by searching for the wounded self that will hesitate, but by recognizing that there is no such self, and that the only meaningful intervention is to dismantle the object he serves. Dismantle the Skull-line, and what remains is a feral seventeen-year-old with forty-year-old skills — dangerous, but no longer organized, and therefore, for the first time in his adult life, *fightable on level ground*.

— END EXECUTIVE BRIEF.


## Chronology I — Origin & Childhood

# CHRONOLOGY I — ORIGIN & CHILDHOOD
## Subject: Brock Rumlow — The Ground Floor

---

### Preface to the Reconstruction

The childhood record on Brock Rumlow is, by the standards of a full-surveillance dossier, *thin in document but thick in inference*. No birth certificate has ever been canonically reproduced; no parents have been named in any panel from *Captain America* vol.1 #359 (Gruenwald, Nov 1989) through the *Secret Empire* run (Spencer, 2016-17); no school records, no childhood photographs, no clergy, no pediatrician, no extended kin. The pre-Crims years are functionally a redacted file. What we possess is the small handful of references Gruenwald seeded into the original Crossbones introduction and the Bloodstone Hunt arc (Cap #357-362), the retrospective material developed in the *Captain America* #400-series and the Diamondback flashback sequences, and the implicit but consistent biographical scaffolding Brubaker preserved when he reactivated the character in 2005.

We work, therefore, the way a competent field office works a sparse file: we triangulate from the adolescent record backward, we read the body of the adult for the imprint of the child, and we hold open the gaps as gaps rather than filling them with confection. What follows is what the record sustains, marked where it is canon and marked where it is *substantiated inference* — the kind of inference an analyst is paid to make and to defend.

---

### 1. Birth, Naming, and the Vanishing Origin

**Name.** Brock Rumlow. The forename is canon from first appearance (Cap #359); the surname is established in the same arc. No middle name has ever been published. The aliases — Crossbones, Bender, Brixton Rumlow, and the disambiguated Frank Simpson variant — are all post-adolescent acquisitions and belong to later chronology files; in this section the subject is exclusively *Brock*.

**Date of birth.** Unfixed in canon. Working from sliding-timeline conventions and the adult record (a man whose adolescence is gang-era Lower East Side, whose mercenary maturity coincides with the late-Cold-War period of his first appearance, and who reads in panel as a man in his late twenties to early thirties at debut), the analytically defensible window for birth is *late 1950s to mid-1960s*, with the most economical placement late 1950s if one preserves publication-era chronology and mid-1960s under modern sliding-scale convention. For surveillance-file purposes we record the date as **UNKNOWN; estimated DOB window with operational confidence**.

**Place of birth.** Almost certainly New York City; the Lower East Side identification (Gruenwald, established in the Crims origin material) is consistent with a born-and-raised pattern rather than an in-migration. There is no canon trace of a hometown elsewhere, no accent shift in his speech registers, no nostalgia for any other geography. His mental map of *home* is Manhattan south of Houston, east of the Bowery — the late-1970s/early-1980s pre-gentrification version of those blocks.

**Parents.** Unnamed. Unshown. Unmentioned by the subject in any documented monologue across thirty-five years of appearances. This is itself a datum: most characters in the Marvel rogues' index have at some point been given a mother to hate, a father to avenge, a sibling to mourn. Rumlow has none. The silence is total and consistent across writers, which suggests it is not an oversight but a structural choice — the character was conceived without a household behind him, and successive custodians have honored that vacancy.

**Inference from the vacancy.** A child who reaches adolescence already capable of leading a sexual assault and committing multiple homicides without any documented adult intervention, protection, or pursuit is a child whose household either (a) did not exist as a functional unit, (b) existed but was non-protective to the point of irrelevance, or (c) was itself a source of the predation that the child later reproduced. The record does not let us choose definitively among these, but it permits us to exclude the alternative: there was no protective adult in the early life. If there had been one, the adolescent conduct would have been impossible at the scale and impunity at which it occurred. The Crims-era Brock operates as a *parentless* organism within the gang ecology, and there is no later evidence of any returning kin — no funeral he attends, no Christmas he marks, no relative leveraged against him by an enemy in three and a half decades of stories. Operationally we record: **no living protective kin at adolescence; no extant kin contact in adulthood**.

---

### 2. The Lower East Side as Developmental Substrate

The neighborhood matters. The Lower East Side of Rumlow's childhood — depending on the dating window, anywhere from the late-Lindsay fiscal-crisis years through the Koch-era heroin and crack escalations — was one of the densest concentrations of organized adolescent street violence in the continental United States. Loisaida, Alphabet City, the blocks east of Avenue A: the documented gang ecology included Latin and Black sets, white-ethnic remnant crews, and a churn of smaller predatory cliques operating in the interstitial real estate of abandoned tenements and city-owned shells. Gruenwald's invented **Savage Crims** sits inside this ecology as a plausible smaller white-ethnic crew, the kind that would have to be unusually vicious to hold turf against larger organizations.

**Schooling.** No record. He is functionally literate in the adult years (reads ops briefings, signs tradecraft, comprehends and uses Hydra and Skull-faction ideological registers without prompting) but shows no trace of formal education beyond the basics. No higher-education references, no professional credentialing, no second language confirmed in canon despite extensive operational time abroad. This is consistent with a truancy-then-dropout profile common to the pre-incarceration trajectory of his peer cohort.

**Material conditions.** Inferred from the gang-affiliation pathway: poverty, household instability, food insecurity at least episodically, exposure to street drug markets as ambient environment rather than personal use. The adult Rumlow's *body discipline* — the absence of substance abuse, the conditioning, the regulated pleasures — is the inverse formation of a childhood spent watching what dissipation does. He is not a man who learned to drink in his father's living room; he is a man who learned, somewhere, that the people who drink and use lose. That lesson, in that neighborhood, was free and constantly demonstrated.

**Religious formation.** None documented. No Catholic markers (no rosary in personal effects, no muttered prayer under duress, no Marian invective when injured — all of which would surface across thirty years of fight-scene dialogue if present). No Jewish markers despite the geography. Functionally areligious from the earliest accessible record; the later devotional structure he develops around the Skull-line is, behaviorally, the first religious-grade attachment in his life.

---

### 3. The Savage Crims — The First Real Family

This is the earliest *documented* phase of Rumlow's life. Gruenwald established the Crims in the Bloodstone-era Crossbones backstory (Cap #359-362 and reinforced in the #400-series flashback material) as a Lower East Side street gang that Rumlow joins as a teenager and within which he rises to leadership. The chronology compresses what was likely a multi-year ascent into a paragraph of exposition, but the operational facts are stable across retellings.

**Age of entry.** Inferable as early-to-mid adolescence — twelve to fourteen — consistent with the regional norm for gang affiliation in that era and necessary to account for his being established as the leader by approximately seventeen, when the homicide sequence forces his exit.

**Role progression within the Crims.** Member → enforcer → leader. The speed of this progression is itself the diagnostic. Most adolescent gang hierarchies are stable on a multi-year basis at each step; for Rumlow to climb from initiate to set-leader inside the window the canon permits, he had to be (a) unusually willing to use force, (b) unusually competent at it, and (c) unusually unbothered by the social cost of using it on other members of his own crew. All three traits are confirmed by the adult record. The gang was, in the most precise sense, his first command — and he commanded it the way he later commanded Skull strike teams: through demonstrated willingness to do what others would not.

**The Crims as attachment surrogate.** With no functional family of origin in the record, the Crims fill the position. But the Crims are a *predatory* peer group, organized hierarchically by capacity for violence, in which affection is expressed through shared offending and loyalty is measured by willingness to harm outsiders together. This is the *only* model of belonging Rumlow learns. It is not modified by any later experience. Every subsequent adult attachment — to Taskmaster's academy as senior instructor, to the Red Skull as field commander, to Sin as partner-and-Skull-successor, even to Hydra-Cap in *Secret Empire* — replicates the Crims structure: a hierarchical predatory in-group bonded by shared violence against designated outsiders. *He never learned another shape of attachment because he was never exposed to one.* The Skull, decades later, gets to play father not because he displaces a prior father but because the slot has been vacant the whole time and the Crims-era leader-of-the-crew role only filled the lateral, not the vertical.

**The girl he loved, allegedly.** A note worth holding open: the Diamondback torture arc contains a moment in which Rumlow frames his obsession in the vocabulary of *love*, and there are scattered intimations across the Crims material that he may have understood himself, in the adolescent gang context, to have had a girl — a Crims-adjacent girlfriend, never named on-panel. The pattern in his adult conduct (women as possessions, "love" as captivity) suggests that whatever the adolescent template was, it was already a possession-template. If there was a first girl, she was *his* in the proprietary sense before she was *with him* in any mutual sense. The record will not let us name her; the structure she occupied is visible in every later woman in his file.

---

### 4. The Founding Atrocity — The Crims Incident

The single most consequential childhood event in the canon, and the one that ends childhood entirely, is the assault-and-homicide sequence Gruenwald established as the reason Rumlow had to flee the country. The bare facts as published:

- Rumlow, leading the Crims, participates in a **gang sexual assault** on a young woman, the sister of a rival.
- In the same operational window, the Crims **murder members of the rival's family**.
- The victims' **father and sister survive long enough to come for revenge** (the canon is most explicit that the father and the sister both confront him).
- Rumlow **kills the father and beats the sister into a coma**.
- He then **flees New York and ultimately the United States**, surfacing later at Taskmaster's mercenary academy.

This sequence is the founding atrocity of the dossier. It happens, on the available chronology, in the late-adolescent window — most economically placed at approximately age seventeen, possibly as late as eighteen or nineteen. Several features deserve granular treatment:

**The sexual component is collective, not solitary.** He leads the assault as group action. This is consistent with the Crims-as-attachment-substrate analysis: even his predation is *bonded* predation. He is not, at this stage, the lone-stalker typology; he is the *captain* of a violent collective performing violence as a collective ritual. His later solo sadism (Diamondback captivity) is the privatization of what began as a gang practice — he kept the practice and discarded the gang.

**The retaliatory homicides are direct and personal.** When the family comes for him, he does not flee them — he meets them and kills them. The father is killed; the sister is left in a coma, an attempted murder by beating. The behavioral signature here is *the same one the adult Crossbones shows in every brawl thereafter*: contact violence, hands and impact, the satisfaction in the proximity. He does not pick up a gun for this confrontation, by the strongest reading of the material; he goes through the family with his body. This is the founding instance of what becomes his lifelong combat preference for close-quarters work even when better tools are available.

**The coma, not the kill, is the tell.** He killed the father outright; he left the sister alive but destroyed. The asymmetric outcome is not random. It is the first surfacing of the pattern that defines his interpersonal violence forever after: men he disposes of, women he *ruins and keeps* in some form short of death. The sister-in-coma is the structural ancestor of Diamondback-in-captivity is the structural ancestor of every woman he ever touches in the record. The template is set at seventeen and never modified.

**The post-event affect is operational, not emotional.** He does not turn himself in, he does not collapse, he does not flee blind — he *exits the country*. That is a planful response under acute pressure, executed by an adolescent who has just committed multiple felonies including homicide. There is no documented evidence in any later flashback or monologue of guilt regarding this sequence. He does not name the victims, does not visit graves, does not avoid the neighborhood when adult business takes him back to New York. The act is *closed* in his internal file the moment it is completed. This is the earliest accessible demonstration of the affective signature that the adult workup identifies: cruelty discharged outward, no residue carried.

**Forensic note on the absence of pursuit.** A multiple-homicide perpetrator who flees the country at seventeen and is never extradited, never tracked by NYPD or federal authorities back to the Crims murders even after becoming an internationally famous costumed terrorist, implies one of two things: either the original case went cold because the victim family was itself sufficiently marginal that the homicides did not receive sustained investigative attention (plausible for the LES of that era), or the case file was buried/lost in the chaos of pre-digital records. Either way, the impunity Rumlow learned at seventeen — that you can do this and walk out of the country and never answer for it — is a foundational lesson that scaffolds every later atrocity. He learns at the outset of adulthood that consequences are something that happens to *other people*.

---

### 5. Formative Bonds, Such As They Are

Bonds in the standard developmental sense — caretakers, siblings, teachers, mentors, friends — are absent from the record. What functions in the bond-slot during the childhood-and-adolescent window is structurally distinct:

**The Crims collective.** Bond-as-co-offending. Not individuated; the gang is a single object to which he is attached. No specific Crim member has ever been named as friend or rival in the canon.

**The victims as inverse-bonds.** The family he destroys at seventeen is the first set of *named-other-humans-with-faces-he-saw* in his accessible record, and he experiences them by destroying them. This is the relational frame he carries forward: the people who matter most concretely to him are the ones he has hurt most concretely. The Diamondback obsession is legible only in this frame — she is bonded to him by what he did to her, not by what passed between them.

**Absences worth recording.** No mentor figure pre-Taskmaster. No older male in the Crims-era record who taught him fighting; he seems to have acquired the foundational skills by doing. No clergy, no coach, no employer, no police-or-probation contact who left a mark. The adult Rumlow's deference to authority is reserved exclusively for the Skull-line; there is no pattern of early submission to legitimate authority that the Skull merely inherits. The Skull is the first vertical attachment of his life — which is why it is total.

---

### 6. Earliest Behavioral Patterns — The Templates Set Before Twenty

By the time Brock Rumlow leaves the United States in his late teens, the entire behavioral architecture of the adult Crossbones is already operational. Itemized:

1. **Violence as primary problem-solving instrument.** Established by the retaliatory homicides; never modified.
2. **Close-quarters combat preference.** Established by the same; he goes through the family with his body, not a weapon.
3. **Planful exit under post-violence pressure.** Established by the flight from New York; this is the same competence that lets him plan multi-stage operations as an adult.
4. **Affective non-residue after killing.** Established by the absence of any post-incident psychiatric or behavioral disturbance; he closes the file the moment the body is on the floor.
5. **Sexual coercion as relational dialect.** Established by the group assault; refined and privatized in adulthood.
6. **Asymmetric disposition of male and female victims.** Men killed; women destroyed-and-kept. Established by the father-killed/sister-comatose pair; recapitulated lifelong.
7. **Collective predation as attachment mode.** Established by Crims membership and leadership; transferred wholesale to Taskmaster academy, Skull's strike forces, Hydra cells.
8. **Hierarchical ascent through demonstrated willingness.** Established by his rise to Crims leader; replicated in every subsequent organization he joins.
9. **Impunity-expectation.** Established by the un-prosecuted Crims homicides; informs his lifelong tactical risk-taking — he genuinely does not expect to be held to account in the ordinary way.
10. **The absence of a non-violent self.** This is the deepest pattern, and the one for which the childhood record provides the strongest evidence by its very emptiness. We cannot point to a phase of his life in which he was not already this. The dossier's recurring conclusion — that his violence *is* his inner life rather than expressing one — is grounded here, in the fact that the earliest accessible Brock Rumlow is already, recognizably, the man who will wear the skull-faced mask for the rest of his life.

---

### 7. Analytic Summary of the Origin File

The ground floor of Brock Rumlow is a vacancy where a family should be, a street ecology in which a predatory peer collective filled the vacancy, and an adolescent atrocity that closed the door on any other developmental trajectory. There is no traumatic *event* in the standard clinical sense that "made" him — no abuse-incident, no parent-death scene, no single rupture — and analytic temptation should be resisted to invent one. What the record sustains is something both more banal and more chilling: a child grew up *without the formative inputs that would have produced a different adult*, and at seventeen he committed acts that foreclosed any remaining alternative path, and he left the country to become a professional version of what he already was.

He did not become Crossbones because of his childhood. He became Crossbones because his childhood did not contain the resistance that would have stopped him from becoming Crossbones. The distinction is forensically essential. The Skull, met in early adulthood, did not create the structure; he *organized* it. Taskmaster, met somewhere between New York and the Skull, did not create the technical competence; he *credentialed* it. The mask, decades later, did not create the face beneath it; it *ratified* it.

The origin file closes, accordingly, with the subject seventeen years old, a multiple killer, on a plane or a freighter out of the country, with no luggage of conscience and no protective person on the receiving end. The next chronology file — Exile, Taskmaster, and the Approach to the Skull — opens on the landing.

— END CHRONOLOGY I.


## Chronology II — Formation & Emergence

# CHRONOLOGY II — FORMATION & EMERGENCE

*Subject: Brock Rumlow / Crossbones. Period covered: approximately age 12 through age 24 — the Lower East Side adolescence, the Savage Crims years, the homicides that ended his New York existence, the period of flight, the apprenticeship at the Taskmaster academy, and the inflection at which the Red Skull's recruiters located him and brought him into the apparatus that would define the remaining four decades of his life. This section reconstructs not merely the chronology but the textures: streets, smells, routines, the micro-decisions a surveillance file would catalogue if such a file had ever been opened on the boy before he became the symbol.*

---

## I. The Pre-Crims Year (approximate age 12–14): Lower East Side, late adolescence onset

The earliest reliably reconstructable window opens with the subject already in the streets — there is no documented household, no school registration that survives in any canonical mention, no recorded guardian. The published record (Gruenwald, *Captain America* #359-362; expansions in #400-series flashbacks) treats the family of origin as a structural absence, and this absence is itself diagnostic data: the boy moves into the gang-ecology of the Lower East Side without anyone in the world functioning as a counter-pull. There is no curfew to violate, no dinner table to be late to, no adult voice in the back of his head he is rebelling against. He is not running *from* a home; he is running *in* an environment that contains no home.

The micro-routines of this period — inferable from the New York of the late 1970s and the geography the canon places him in — are the small predations of a fatherless boy in a Manhattan that had not yet been remade: petty theft from corner stores, the running of errands for older boys, sleeping in stairwells when weather permitted, the bodega ecology of cigarettes and coffee and small loans against future violence. He learns very early what a surveillance file would later call **his baseline operational tempo**: long stretches of waiting, watching, conserving, punctuated by short bursts of decisive physical action. This tempo never changes for the rest of his life. The man who would later sit, motionless, on a Brooklyn rooftop for nine hours waiting for Steve Rogers to climb the courthouse steps was rehearsed in stairwells thirty years before, waiting for an older boy to leave a hallway so a wallet could be lifted.

Physically, the subject's adolescent development outpaces his peers. By thirteen he is the size of a sixteen-year-old; by fifteen he is, by every available description, the largest and strongest boy on his block. This precocity is the substrate of everything that follows. He learns, before he learns anything else, that his body resolves disputes. The cognitive sequence that should normally develop in middle adolescence — argue, negotiate, concede, retry — is replaced by a foreshortened sequence: **observe, close distance, strike, conclude.** No subsequent education ever installs the missing middle. The Taskmaster academy will refine the striking; the Red Skull will supply the rationale; nobody will ever teach him to argue.

A surveillance file would note here the absence of any documented mentor in the pre-Crims period. He has no boxing coach, no priest, no shop teacher, no older cousin in a uniform. The first older men to take an interest in him are the leadership of the Savage Crims.

---

## II. Entry to the Savage Crims (approximate age 14–15)

The Crims, as the canon establishes them, are a working street gang of the Lower East Side, not a national organization — turf-based, ethnically mixed, organized around the standard hierarchy of an older "president," a war-captain, and a body of soldiers and apprentices. The subject enters at the bottom and rises with anomalous speed. The published account makes him gang leader by approximately seventeen, which means the climb from initiate to top of a violent peer hierarchy takes roughly two to three years — a velocity that requires either an unusual disposition or an unusual capacity, and in his case clearly both.

The micro-behaviors of the ascent are reconstructable from his later operational signature. He does not, in any documented adult engagement, fight emotionally; he fights to a plan. The Crims ascent therefore was almost certainly not won by being the *angriest* boy in the gang (Lower East Side gangs of the period had no shortage of angrier boys) but by being the *coldest* — the one who could be told to hurt someone next Tuesday and would arrive Tuesday afternoon with the route mapped, the implement chosen, the alibi pre-laid. The other Crims would have learned, within months of his arrival, that Brock did the jobs nobody else wanted to do and did them without theater and without recourse. This is the prototype of every relationship he forms thereafter with a superior: *give me the task and I will return with the body.* The Red Skull, ten years later, recognizes the disposition instantly because the disposition has been finished work for a decade.

Within the Crims, three behavioral templates are laid down that will persist for the rest of his life:

1. **Hierarchy as the only legible social structure.** He understands up and down. He does not understand sideways. The Crims have a president, and the president has lieutenants, and the lieutenants have soldiers, and this geometry feels, to him, like the natural shape of human relations. He will reproduce it in every subsequent affiliation. When placed in environments lacking this structure he becomes restless and corrosive; he generates a hierarchy if none is provided.

2. **Sexual conduct as predation within the hierarchy's permissions.** The Crims practice the sexual violence permitted to gangs of their type and period; the subject participates and, by the canonical record, leads. He does not learn, in adolescence, a model of sexual exchange that is not coercive. There is no documented teenage girlfriend, no first love, no flirtation in the ordinary sense. The first sexual experiences encoded in the file are the assaults committed with the Crims on a rival gang member's female relations. This is the soil out of which, six or seven years later, his treatment of Rachel Leighton grows; the Diamondback captivity is not a deviation, it is the executive version of the adolescent default.

3. **Violence as identity-production, not identity-expression.** The other Crims become violent; the subject *becomes Crims-violent*. The gang's reputation becomes the medium through which he constructs a self. He is, even at sixteen, less an angry boy than a boy assembling a feared figure. The skull-mask of twenty years later is the same project at higher resolution. The choice to terrify is already the choice he is making at fifteen, when he learns that a rumor of his cruelty does the work of an actual beating.

---

## III. The Originary Crime (approximate age 16–17)

The single event that ends the New York life: the Crims, with the subject leading, raid the family of a rival — the canonical text establishes a sexual assault and the murder of the rival's family members. The granular sequence implied by the published account is: planning, entry, sexual violence, killing, exit. The duration cannot be precisely established but the operation has the texture of a sustained intrusion, not a drive-by. He is in the home long enough to do everything that is done. The behavioral data this episode generates are:

- He is not destabilized by killing. The act, on the page and in every later restatement, is followed by no documented psychological disturbance — no flight to a confessor, no drinking binge, no nightmares mentioned in any subsequent flashback. The killing files smoothly into the day.

- He is not destabilized by the sexual violence either. There is no shame-spiral, no compensatory religiosity, no withdrawal from sexual behavior. The conduct enters the catalogue of permitted personal acts and remains there.

- He is destabilized — slightly, briefly, operationally — by the *consequence*: the rival's father and sister come for him. This is the only moment in the entire adolescent record in which he is *reacted to* by an adult force seeking to do him violence. He kills both. He puts the sister into a coma. The micro-detail to note: he does not flee from the father and sister; he *engages* and ends them. The flight comes after, and is from the *city*, not from the *fight*. He has never, before or since, fled an opponent in front of him; he flees only systems and territories.

What the surveillance file would have to note here, and what the canonical material implies through omission, is the absence of any **transitional ritual**. There is no goodbye. He does not visit anyone. He does not leave a letter. He does not retrieve a possession. The exit from New York is geographically total and psychologically frictionless. He is already a man whose attachments are to a *role*, not to *persons or places*, and the role is portable. He carries it onto whichever plane or freighter takes him out, and lands with it intact in whatever country first receives him.

---

## IV. The Exile Interval (approximate age 17–19/20)

This is the least documented stretch of the subject's life and therefore the period in which a surveillance file would be densest with inference. The canon places him, by the end of the interval, at the Taskmaster academy — meaning the years between flight and academy-arrival were spent acquiring at least the credibility necessary for the academy to take him.

The likely textures of this period, reconstructed from the surrounding evidence:

**Movement.** A teenager wanted for multiple homicides in New York and arriving, eventually, in the freelance-criminal training ecosystem implies a passage through the mercenary undercurrents of Central America, the Mediterranean, or West Africa — the period's standard reservoirs of work for unattached young men with capacity for violence and no documentation. He learns, in this interval, the small-craft survival skills that mark his later career: the management of false papers; the discipline of leaving no possessions in any room he sleeps in; the habit of orienting himself, immediately upon arrival anywhere, to the room's two exits and the building's roof access. None of these are taught at Taskmaster's academy; all of them are present in his operational signature when he gets there.

**First contract work.** He almost certainly takes paid violence assignments in this period — the standard entry stratum of bodyguard work, debt collection, contracted assault. The behavioral conditioning here is critical: *violence becomes wage labor*. The link between cruelty and money is forged. From this point onward he never does anything cruel that is not also paid for or sanctioned by a superior. The sadism does not become *less*; it becomes *housed*. This is what later allows him to look, to the casual observer, like a professional rather than a maniac. The sadism is on a leash held by the contract.

**The language acquisition.** By the time he surfaces in the published record as a Taskmaster instructor, the subject is operational across borders. He has, almost certainly, acquired functional fragments of at least Spanish and German in the exile period, possibly Arabic. These are not the languages of scholarship; they are the languages of *transaction* — order a drink, name a price, tell a man to lie down.

**The body project begins.** The physical conditioning that defines his adult silhouette is not a gym product; it is the product of these wandering years. He is in motion, fighting often, eating roughly, sleeping in postures that build the spinal compensations he will carry into middle age. The musculature is functional, not aesthetic. He never, at any documented later point, trains for appearance; the body is a tool that has been used into its shape.

What does *not* happen in this interval is any documented attachment. No companion, no lover, no protégé. He is alone for two or three years and the aloneness does not deform him because he had no template of non-aloneness to lose. This is the period that confirms, structurally, that he will never form lateral bonds. He had the developmental window in which young men ordinarily form their first peer-friendships outside the family; he spent it moving across borders alone. The window closes; it does not reopen.

---

## V. The Taskmaster Academy (approximate age 19/20–22)

He arrives, the published record indicates, as a student; he leaves as the senior instructor. This is the most important professional transformation of his life, and it occurs in roughly two to three years.

The academy itself, as the canon establishes it, is a fee-for-service training facility for low- and mid-tier criminal operatives — a place where henchmen are made. Taskmaster's own pedagogical method is observational: he learns by watching and reproduces with fidelity. The subject is therefore taught by a man whose strength is *imitation of excellence*, which is precisely what the subject needs, because his pre-academy skill set is the unsupervised brawling of a Lower East Side boy. The academy converts him from a gifted thug into a *technician*.

The granular acquisitions in this period:

- **Firearms across the catalogue.** He becomes competent with handguns, long guns, submachine guns, the standard infantry weapons; he develops the *sniping* capacity that will, six or seven years later, be deployed against Captain America on the courthouse steps. The sniper habit — long stillness, controlled breathing, the willingness to wait — is the academy's most lasting gift to him because it operationalizes a temperamental tendency he already had. He was a patient boy; he becomes a patient shooter.

- **Edged weapons.** Knives, bayonet work, the use of improvised cutting tools. His later mask-and-blade signature in close combat is sourced here.

- **Demolitions.** This is novel acquisition for him; the academy gives him a working competence with conventional and shaped charges that will mark every subsequent strike-team operation he commands. He does not become a demolitions specialist in the artisan sense, but he becomes capable enough to plan around explosives without requiring a separate technician for routine work.

- **Hand-to-hand at professional grade.** The academy's hand-to-hand curriculum — eclectic, drawn from Taskmaster's photographic absorption of the planet's combat traditions — gives the subject a vocabulary far beyond the brawling he arrived with. He never becomes, in the strict sense, a martial *artist* — there is no documented evidence he absorbed the philosophical or aesthetic strata of any tradition — but he becomes a hand-to-hand *operator* of a high order. He can fight any of the standard opposition typologies and adapt mid-engagement.

- **Tradecraft.** Surveillance and counter-surveillance, dead drops, the disciplines of professional anonymity. He becomes the man who can walk a route twice without appearing to have walked it once.

The promotion to senior instructor is the inflection. It tells us two things the published record otherwise only implies: he is, by his early twenties, *capable of teaching* — meaning he has both the technical mastery and the analytic capacity to break a skill into reproducible parts — and he is, by Taskmaster's judgment, *reliable*. Taskmaster is not in the business of letting unstable men teach his students; the choice of the subject as senior instructor is a market signal that he is, by criminal-professional standards, governable. The Skull's recruiters will read this signal when they read it.

The instructor period also produces, for the first time in his life, a *vertical* relationship that is not predatory in either direction. Taskmaster is his superior and uses him; the subject is competent and serves. This is the rehearsal of the Skull-relationship. The template — *a fearsome older man with a mask, who teaches and uses me* — is laid down here, and the Skull, when he arrives, slots into a slot the academy carved.

What does not happen at the academy: there is no documented relationship with any fellow student or instructor that survives the period. He makes no professional friend at Taskmaster's. He makes no enemy either. He passes through the institution and leaves nothing personal behind, which is precisely the conduct of a man who has, by twenty-two, fully internalized that institutions are passages, not homes.

---

## VI. Recruitment by the Red Skull (approximate age 22–23)

The Skull's apparatus identifies him through the channels by which such apparatuses identify men of his type — instructor pools at facilities like Taskmaster's are the recruiting grounds of every authoritarian operation that needs hand-grade violence above thug grade and below super-soldier grade. The Skull is looking, in this period, for a *field commander*: a man who can lead strike teams, take orders, and serve as the personal hand of the leader without ever being suspected of seeking the leader's chair.

The subject is, by the candidate metrics, almost too good a fit. The recruiter's notes a competent intelligence service would have generated would read: *young, fluent in violence, demonstrably governable, no extant attachments to compromise, no family to leverage against him, no religion, no ideology of his own that would interfere with assimilation to ours, physically anomalous in size and capacity, instructor-tested, exile-tested, kill-tested before the age of eighteen.* He is the Skull's ideal raw material. The Skull, who is among the most discerning recruiters in the criminal world of his generation, recognizes this within one or two interviews.

The behavioral data of the recruitment itself are unrecorded but inferable. The subject does not negotiate. He does not ask about pay or terms beyond what is necessary to function. He commits in the first conversation and the commitment is total. He has been waiting, since the Crims, for a hierarchy worthy of his capacity; the Skull is the first man whose hierarchy is *large* enough.

The micro-behaviors that begin in this period and persist for the next thirty years on his record:

- **Address.** He addresses the Skull with a deference that has no equivalent anywhere else in his life. The voice register drops; the eye contact pattern changes; he is, with the Skull, a younger man.

- **Proximity.** He arranges his physical position, in any room containing the Skull, so that his body is between the Skull and the room's most likely threat vector. He does this without being asked and continues to do it for the entire duration of the relationship. It is the first reliable evidence that he experiences the Skull-protection as a *vocation*, not a job.

- **Silence.** He does not speak unless spoken to in the Skull's presence — a discipline he extends to no other superior. With Taskmaster he had been an instructor who could disagree on technique. With the Skull he becomes a man who has no opinions until asked for them.

- **The reading project.** It is in this period, inferable from his later capacity to function in the Skull's ideological environment without embarrassment, that he absorbs the working vocabulary of the Skull's worldview — the Nietzschean tropes, the master-slave framings, the contempt for liberal modernity. He does not read deeply; he reads *enough*. The reading is for parroting and for *recognition* of the Skull's references, not for independent thought. This is the period in which he becomes capable of *housing* his sadism in an ideology, which is what allows him to be promoted from field commander to Crossbones.

---

## VII. The Emergence of Crossbones (approximate age 23–24)

The persona is not handed to him; he constructs it, with the Skull's evident approval, over a period of months. The components, sequentially:

1. **The name.** "Crossbones" is the subject's choice, or at least his early adoption — a name that announces death and theatricality. He selects, over the available alternatives, the one that is most *symbolic* and least *personal*. The man who in childhood had no protective adult around to name him properly now names himself after a piece of pirate iconography. The childishness of the choice is itself diagnostic; he is, despite the violence, still operating within an adolescent imaginary about what frightens.

2. **The skull aesthetic.** The skull motif is, of course, derivative — derivative of the Red Skull whose servant he is — and the derivation is intentional. He brands himself as the Skull's instrument by wearing the Skull's symbol on his face. This is the first systematic act of *identification with the patron* in his life. It will only intensify after the disfigurement, which converts the affiliation from emblem to flesh.

3. **The tactical kit.** The harness, the boots, the layered gear — assembled in this period to a specification that, once set, the subject barely modifies for the rest of his career. The kit's signature is *functional excess*: he carries more than he needs, of better quality than the operation requires, because the kit is also the costume and the costume must read at distance. The boy who learned in the Crims that rumor does the work of beating has become the man who lets his silhouette do the work of his entrance.

4. **The body of work.** Within months of the Crossbones designation, he is executing the operations that will define his early reputation in the Skull's organization — strike-team leadership, hostage management, the wet work that other commanders won't authorize. He establishes, in this period, the operational signature he will carry into every subsequent decade: *plan tight, wait long, strike short, leave clean, dominate the survivors with theater.*

The first defining choice of the Crossbones era — and the one whose fallout extends across the entire subsequent published record — is the **kidnapping and captivity of Diamondback**, which occurs only a few years after the Crossbones persona consolidates. The capture is presented, by the subject and within his own internal narration, as an *operational* matter (she is a defector who must be retrieved or punished), but the conduct during the captivity exposes that it is also, and primarily, a *personal* matter to him. He extends the captivity beyond operational necessity. He performs the captivity for his own gratification. He invests in her terror as if it were a project. He fails — she is recovered by Captain America's people — and the failure inscribes itself permanently into his psychological architecture. For the remaining decades of his career, Rachel Leighton is the *unfinished possession*, the one variable his apparatus did not close. The Diamondback episode is the early adulthood event that reveals, conclusively, that the sadism is not subordinated to the work; the sadism is *coextensive* with the work, and when the two conflict the sadism wins.

The second defining choice of the period is **the refusal to seek autonomy from the Skull**. He has, by twenty-four, every credential needed to operate independently: combat reputation, network, kit, resources. He could become his own contractor; many of his peers do. He does not. He chooses, instead, to deepen his service. The choice is so consistent across the subsequent record that it ceases to look like a choice and begins to look like a structure — but the structure was set in this early window, when the alternative was still live. He could have left the Skull at twenty-four. He did not even consider it. The bond is, by this point, the central organizing fact of his interior life, and will remain so until death.

---

## VIII. Fallout and Forward Trajectory

By the end of this formative arc — somewhere around the subject's twenty-fourth year — every structural feature of the adult Crossbones is in place:

- The hierarchical relational geometry, with the Skull-line as the singular upward attachment, is locked.
- The sadistic specifier is operational and housed within contracted violence, which gives it both license and durability.
- The technical kit — firearms, blade, demolitions, hand-to-hand, tradecraft — is at professional grade and will only be refined, not transformed, by subsequent experience.
- The persona, the silhouette, the name, the mask-aesthetic are constructed and will only be *intensified* by the later disfigurement, not redirected.
- The capacity for lateral attachment is foreclosed, the developmental window having closed during the exile interval.
- The Diamondback grudge is initiated and will run, as an unresolved sub-routine, beneath the entire subsequent record.
- The pattern of *organized* rather than *chaotic* antisociality is established; he will be, for the rest of his life, the dangerous kind of monster — the one with a calendar.

The formation period does not so much *produce* Brock Rumlow as *finish* him. The boy who entered the Crims at fourteen and the man who emerged from the Taskmaster academy at twenty-two are recognizably the same person; the Skull's recruitment supplies the final scaffold — the worthy patron, the legible cause, the permanent address — into which an already-completed temperament can move and live.

Everything that follows in the published record — the Steve Rogers assassination, the disfigurement, the Skadi service, the Xavier-funeral atrocity, the Pleasant Hill interlude, the Hydra-Cap fealty — is the unfolding of a struct


## Chronology III — The Defining Middle Period

# Chronology III — The Defining Middle Period

*Operational window: roughly the late Gruenwald arc through Brubaker's complete tenure and into the Fear Itself prelude — the years during which the subject ceases to be a useful enforcer and becomes the singular instrument he is now remembered as. This is the longest behaviorally legible stretch of the file, and the period in which every later pattern is laid down.*

---

## 6.1 — The Diamondback Years: Possession as Doctrine

The middle period opens with what the file must treat as the foundational interpersonal episode of the subject's adult life: the abduction, captivity, and attempted breaking of Rachel Leighton (Diamondback) after her defection from the Serpent Society to Captain America (Cap #393–408 arc; "The Superia Stratagem" and surrounding issues). This is not a one-off. It is a multi-issue, multi-location course of conduct — a yacht, a remote facility, a transfer of custody to and from Skull-aligned safehouses — and the subject's own behavior across it constitutes the most complete behavioral specimen we have of him outside combat.

Granular notes, reverse-engineered from the record:

- He addresses her by first name almost exclusively during captivity and by codename in front of subordinates — a code-switch consistent with the *ownership* schema in §3. To others she is the prisoner; to him she is *Rachel*, which he experiences as intimacy.
- He provides her food himself rather than delegating. The file flags this not as kindness but as territorial marking — the keeper feeds the animal.
- He oscillates on a short cycle between threat (graphic, sexually inflected) and what he frames as tenderness (a hand on her face, an unsolicited compliment). She experiences both as the same thing because they are; the file should record this as the subject's earliest documented use of the *idealization-by-force* relational template that recurs whenever he is given prolonged proximity to a target.
- He does not actually rape her on-page during this captivity. This is significant. The restraint is not moral. It is the gambler's restraint: he believes that if he waits, she will *come to him*, and that this consummation will retroactively prove he was loved. The fantasy structure is intact; the fantasy requires her assent. He cannot risk taking what would invalidate the fantasy.
- When she escapes, he does not move on. Across the next ~five years of published material, in every encounter with the Captain America operational sphere, he asks after her, threatens her by name, leaves messages for her — surveillance-grade behaviors that establish a stalking pattern persisting across continents and Skull-orchestrated operations.

Behavioral conclusion for the period: by his late twenties Rumlow has established that he cannot release a possession-coded target. The Diamondback grudge is the first long-running file *within* his file. It will still be operative at his death.

---

## 6.2 — The Skull's Right Hand: Consolidation Under the Father

Across the same window the subject is consolidating his position within the Red Skull's organization to the point of indispensability. The Gruenwald-era Skull (in the cloned-Rogers body) maintains a tiered apparatus — Mother Night and the Sisters of Sin, Machinesmith, Crossbones at field command — and the subject is steadily elevated above peers who began ahead of him. The mechanism is not politicking; the subject is conspicuously *bad* at courtly maneuver. The mechanism is *delivery*. He is the one who returns from operations with the asset, the body, the intelligence. Other lieutenants fail upward through ideology; he fails forward through competence.

Patterns laid down here that persist for the rest of the file:

- **Daily proximity to the Skull.** From this period forward, when the Skull is in residence, the subject is in the next room. He sleeps near. He eats when the Skull eats. The file should treat this as quasi-monastic: a discipline of presence rather than a security posture, because security details rotate and he does not.
- **Refusal of independent command opportunities.** Multiple times in this stretch he is offered operational autonomy (his own cell, his own theater) and declines or accepts only nominally, returning to the Skull's side at the first opportunity. This is the clearest possible data on the subject's actual ambition: he does not want a throne; he wants to stand beside one.
- **The voice-register adjustment.** When speaking to or about the Skull, his speech registers shift — shorter sentences, more formal address, fewer obscenities. He does not curse in the Skull's presence. He curses constantly outside it. This is the most reliable conversational tell in his file for *who he believes is currently in the room with him spiritually*, even when alone.

The Skull's body-deaths and body-swaps across this period (the Kubekult arc, the deaths and returns) do not interrupt the bond. The subject treats discontinuities of the Skull's body as administrative inconveniences. The introject is the man; the meat is incidental. This is doctrinally important: it means the Skull-line will remain a coherent attachment object for him even after the Skull's physical death is canonical, and it forecasts his clean transfer of devotion to Sin (§6.6) and later to Hydra-Cap (§7).

---

## 6.3 — Acts of Vengeance, Streets of Poison, the Bloodstone Hunt: The Middle-Era Operational Tempo

The subject is a peripheral but consistently present operator across the major Gruenwald-era event arcs. He is not a participant in Acts of Vengeance high command — he is *muscle on call*. The Bloodstone Hunt period sees him moving across multiple continents on the Skull's errands; Streets of Poison (the Cap-on-Ice arc) finds him repeatedly in proximity to Rogers without engaging, because the Skull has not authorized engagement.

The pattern across these arcs:

- **Patience under leash.** The subject is in a position to attempt the kill on Captain America more than a dozen times across this stretch and does not, because the order has not come. This is the strongest possible evidence against the prevailing surface impression of him as an undisciplined sadist. He defers gratification at a level most assets cannot. He defers it specifically and only when the Skull is the authorizing entity.
- **Operational geography.** The file should note the routes he establishes in this period — properties used and reused (the Skull's various American and European bastions), a preference for coastal extraction, a tradecraft tic of arriving early at meeting locations and surveilling them for several hours before contact. Subordinates from this era who survive long enough to be debriefed (a small number) describe him as *boring to work with* — a clean professional, minimal conversation, no anecdotes, no jokes outside the sadistic register, no curiosity about subordinates' lives. He learns their names and their capabilities. He does not learn their backgrounds.
- **Treatment of women in the operation.** Mother Night, the Sisters of Sin (pre-Sin's later prominence), various Skull-affiliated female operatives — the subject is correct with them, occasionally formal, never flirtatious. He partitions: women inside the Skull's organization are *not* available to his possession schema, because they belong to the Skull. The schema is therefore not undifferentiated misogyny; it is property recognition. Outside the Skull's umbrella, women are targets. Inside it, they are colleagues whose persons he does not trespass.

---

## 6.4 — The Long Interregnum: Skull-Deaths and the Subject Adrift

There are stretches in the middle period (most pronounced after the Gruenwald-era Skull's apparent destruction and before the Brubaker-era resurrections) when the subject has no living Skull to serve. These are the closest the file ever comes to a *naturalistic experiment* on him: what does this man do when the organizing object is absent?

The record across these intervals shows:

- An immediate uptick in freelance mercenary work. He returns, functionally, to a Taskmaster-instructor-level operative-for-hire. He takes contracts that are beneath him.
- A degradation of tactical patience. The Diamondback obsession, normally background-prioritized below Skull-business, surges to the foreground; this is when his most ill-advised attempts on her occur.
- An increase in personal violence per operation. Without the discipline-supplying object, the sadism runs the operation rather than serving it. Kills get longer. Witnesses pile up. Tradecraft suffers.
- Notably: no depression, no aimlessness in the affective sense. He does not mope. He does not drink. He works. The hollowness is structural, not phenomenological — he does not *feel* the absence; he *operates worse* inside it.

This is the period that most strongly substantiates the central diagnostic claim from §4: that the Skull is the organizing introject and his discipline is borrowed. Strip the organizing object and the structure remains standing but its load-bearing wall is gone. The subject does not collapse. He simply becomes a less effective version of the same man.

---

## 6.5 — Brubaker Entry: The Professionalization

The transition into the Brubaker-era handling (Captain America vol. 5, from 2005) marks the most pronounced *operational* evolution in the file. The subject is now in his thirties-into-forties; the street-killer affect is fully sublimated into a professional veneer. He is read by other professionals — Bucky in particular, in the Winter Soldier arc — as a peer-tier operator, not a thug. His tradecraft sharpens visibly:

- **Weapons profile.** Established preferences from this period: a heavy combat knife carried inverted on the left chest rig; a sidearm carried high-and-tight in a thigh holster, not on the belt; a preference for breaching charges he has built himself rather than issued ordnance. He distrusts ordnance he did not assemble.
- **Comms discipline.** He goes long stretches without verbal communication during operations, using hand signals he developed at the Taskmaster academy. Subordinates from this era report that he speaks in op only to correct an error or order a kill.
- **Vehicle preferences.** Established route habits: he does not take the same route twice within a thirty-day window in any city; he switches vehicles at least once mid-operation; he prefers an extraction driver he has personally vetted and will scrub an op rather than accept an unknown driver. None of this is paranoia; it is *industry standard executed without exception*, which in this industry is rare.
- **Sleep.** He sleeps in four-to-five-hour increments, can fall asleep in transit, wakes at any contact noise instantly. He does not appear to dream in any reportable sense; subordinates who have shared safehouses with him describe him as silent through the night.

The professional veneer is not character growth. The sadism is intact, the schemas are intact, the Skull-bond is intact. What has changed is *finish*. He has spent twenty years in the trade and the rough edges are gone from everything except the cruelty, which has the same rough edges it had at seventeen because cruelty is the part he never wanted to file down.

---

## 6.6 — The Sin Partnership

Across this same Brubaker stretch the subject's partnership with Sinthea Schmidt consolidates from working association into something the file must treat as the single most complete relational bond of his adult life — closer in tenure than Diamondback, more egalitarian than the Skull, and structurally unique in his record.

The bond's geometry:

- She is the Skull's daughter. This makes her, in the subject's internal economy, a continuation of the Skull-line and thus inside the property-recognition partition (§6.3). He cannot, by his own rules, treat her as a possession-target.
- She is also peer-tier in violence — a sadist of comparable wattage, ideologically aligned, operationally capable. This makes her, uniquely in his record, *a peer*. The vertical-only relational pattern from §5 is bent here, but not broken: the file should read Sin as functionally a *junior co-regent of the Skull-line*, allowing him to relate horizontally only because she is vertically authorized.
- The sexual component is real and mutual. The file should not overcode this as romance in any conventional sense. Sex and operational violence are paired stimuli for both; the partnership runs on the same fuel.
- The breakout from SHIELD custody (Cap #25 aftermath) is the test event. She comes for him. This is, as far as the file can determine, the first time in his life anyone has come for him without being ordered to. He does not, behaviorally, register this as the existential datum it would be for most subjects — but his subsequent attachment to her tightens markedly, and his operational subordination to her once she becomes Skadi (Fear Itself) is offered without internal friction.

Diagnostic addendum: the Sin partnership is the only data point in the file that complicates the read of the subject as relationally incapable. The qualification: she succeeded only by being structurally indistinguishable from his master rather than from his peers. The pattern still holds. He has never bonded with an equal who was *only* an equal.

---

## 6.7 — The Assassination of Captain America

The defining single act of the middle period and of the file as a whole. Captain America #25 (2007). The subject pulls the trigger on the rifle round that strikes Rogers on the courthouse steps, as part of a plan architected by the Red Skull and Faustus, with Sharon Carter triggered to deliver the killing follow-up.

The act's behavioral content:

- **Selection of role.** The subject claims the rifle position personally. He is not assigned it; he requests it. The Skull grants it. This is the clearest possible evidence that the Skull understood the symbolic economy of the operation — the longest-tenured personal enemy of Rogers, the man who has spent two decades waiting for permission, given the shot at last.
- **The shot itself.** Clean, single round, at distance, into a crowd, under SHIELD security cordon. Technically excellent. There is no documented hesitation, no documented adrenal overshoot. He took the shot as he had taken every other shot of his career — but this one he had been *saving*.
- **Affect after.** The subject does not celebrate operationally. Captured by SHIELD shortly after, he is, by interrogation accounts, *settled*. The file should read this as the closest he has ever come to phenomenological satisfaction — not joy, not relief, but the completion of a long-deferred task. He has delivered the Skull's central enemy to the Skull's plan. He has, in his own terms, *paid for his place*.
- **The interrogation.** Standard SHIELD methods. He gives essentially nothing. The previously catalogued sleep pattern holds in custody — short cycles, immediate waking. He does not request counsel. He does not bargain. He waits, because he has been told (or has decided) that Sin will come, and she does.

The act is also the file's strongest evidence that the subject is capable of *patience at the scale of decades* when the authorizing object is the Skull. He could have moved on Rogers a hundred times across the preceding twenty years. He did not, because the order had not come. When the order came he executed flawlessly. There is no operator in the rogue catalog who exhibits this profile in this magnitude.

---

## 6.8 — Reborn, the Disfigurement, and the Mask Becoming Face

The "Reborn" sequence and the surrounding Red Skull resurrection arcs deliver the somatic event that physically marks the middle period's end: the subject's face is destroyed by a power discharge from the Skull's reanimated/possessed body. Full-thickness facial and scalp burns, permanent disfigurement, almost certain chronic neuropathic pain (untreated, per the personality-congruent denial flagged in §4).

The behavioral aftermath is the diagnostically critical observation of the entire file:

- **No avoidance response.** No withdrawal, no convalescence beyond the medically necessary minimum, no documented attempt at reconstructive surgery or prosthetic restoration of the *previous* face. He could have pursued any of these and did not.
- **Immediate adoption of the tactical skull mask as continuous wear.** Pre-disfigurement, the mask had been costume — situational, operational, removable. Post-disfigurement it becomes face. Subordinates from this period forward almost never see him unmasked; intimate witnesses (Sin) see the ruin and do not flinch, which the file records as confirmation that the mask is not protection from her gaze but from everyone else's *and* from the symbolic loss of the previous face.
- **Operational tempo increase.** Most subjects with this injury de-escalate for months. He escalates. The work absorbs the pain, and the pain feeds the work. The structure organizes the suffering rather than the other way around.

This is the moment at which Brock Rumlow, residually, ceases to exist as a separate identity beneath the Crossbones identity. The middle period closes with the subject *fully consolidated as the symbol*. Everything from this point forward in the file is the symbol operating, not the man wearing the symbol.

---

## 6.9 — Fear Itself and the Devotional Transfer

The Fear Itself arc and its immediate prologue/sequel material (subject and Sin's pursuit of the Hammer of Skadi; Sin's transformation into Skadi; subject as Skadi's enforcer) close the middle period with the cleanest possible behavioral confirmation of the §6.2 thesis: the Skull-line is the attachment object, not any individual member of it.

The subject's transition from serving the Skull to serving Skadi is *seamless*. There is no period of adjustment, no internal-conflict micro-tells, no protest-then-acceptance arc. He simply continues. The devotion is portable along the bloodline because the devotion was never to the man; it was to the *project*, and Sin-as-Skadi is the project's current vessel. The file should note this with diagnostic emphasis: a subject whose primary attachment is to a *line* rather than a *person* is functionally untreatable through bereavement, capture, or removal of any individual member. The line must be dismantled as a *symbolic structure* to dismantle him.

---

## 6.10 — Patterns Laid Down, Patterns Hardened

By the close of this middle period the file has all the longitudinal material it needs. The following patterns, established in fragments across the early record, are by this point hardened to the point of automaticity and will persist unchanged through the late-period material:

- **The Skull-line devotion** — vertical attachment to the *line* not the individual; survives every discontinuity of body, death, and succession.
- **The possession schema** — applied to outside-the-umbrella women; not applied to inside-the-umbrella women; Diamondback as the singular unresolved instance.
- **The discipline-by-borrowing** — composure and patience are excellent when the Skull-line is the authorizing object, degraded when it is absent.
