He is not loyal to the man; he is loyal to the certification.

**Leverage.** The certification itself. Any operation that could corrupt Rumlow's belief in Skull-line endorsement of the current leader-figure would split him from the command structure. He has no independent ideological commitment to compensate.

---

## VII. ABSENCES OF NOTE (Negative-Space Map)

A complete relational map of this subject must also itemize what is missing, because the absences are diagnostically louder than the presences.

- **No parents on the record.** No surrogate parental figure prior to Schmidt. The Skull therefore occupies an unusually pure father-slot, with no prior fathers to compete or to be compared.
- **No siblings, biological or fictive, outside the gang.** The Savage Crims function as a perverse sibship in adolescence; nothing functionally analogous appears in adulthood. Sin is the closest thing to a sibling-coded figure, but the incest-adjacent geometry of that bond is so dense that calling her a sister-figure understates and mis-describes it; she is *all roles at once* on the Skull-line.
- **No mentor figures outside the criminal-paramilitary ecology.** No teacher, no coach, no clergyman, no civilian adult who once treated him with kindness. The hypothesis is not that no such figure ever existed — the canon is silent — but that none penetrated to a level that left a behavioral residue.
- **No friends.** Across thirty-five years of canon there is not one figure who can be described as a friend in the ordinary sense — someone whose company he seeks for non-instrumental reasons, with whom he discloses, in whose presence he relaxes. Sin is the nearest approximation and remains a Skull-line attachment first.
- **No proteges who became peers.** He has trained operators; none has graduated into peer status with him. The hierarchy he commands does not produce lateral graduates because he does not permit it.
- **No reconciliation figures.** No one in the record represents an opening to a different life; no character offers him an exit ramp he then refuses. The exits do not appear because the canon, correctly, reads him as a man who does not have any.

The shape of the negative space confirms the shape of the positive: a strictly vertical relational world organized around a single line of authority, with no lateral tissue and no civilian periphery. Strategically, this is the most important fact about him after the Skull-bond itself. There is no one to call. There is no one to lose that has not already been accounted for. The leverage is in the line, or it is nowhere.

— END SECTION.


## Relationships III — Rivals, Enemies & Lovers

# RELATIONSHIPS III — RIVALS, ENEMIES & LOVERS

*UATU Dossier, Subject: Brock Rumlow / Crossbones. Cross-referenced to Sections 1–5; supersedes no prior subsection.*

A preliminary note on taxonomy. With most subjects, the categories "rival," "enemy," and "lover" are reasonably discrete; with Rumlow they bleed. He does not relate to anyone except along a dominance axis, which means his enemies and his intimates occupy structurally similar slots — bodies he intends to possess, by penetration or by killing or, in the limit case, by both. His "love" is a captivity script; his "hate" is a captivity script that has not yet acquired a bed. The reader should hold that frame throughout. What separates the lovers from the enemies in his interior file is not the affective tone but the question of *who* he wishes to bring the body back to: himself (intimates), the Skull-line (enemies), or the cause as monument (rivals he wants to leave on display).

The list that follows is exhaustive of the canonically substantiated relational record. Sub-sections are scaled to relational weight, not to story-time minutes.

---

## I. ENEMIES

### 1. STEVE ROGERS — the central enemy, the ideological wound

**History.** Rogers enters Rumlow's life as the Red Skull's standing problem, which makes Rumlow's relationship to Rogers, from inception, *derivative* — he hates Rogers because the Skull hates Rogers, and then over time the derivative hatred fossilizes into something Rumlow experiences as his own. The early Gruenwald-period engagements (Cap #359 onward) are field-tactical: Rumlow as muscle, Rogers as obstacle. Across the late 80s and 90s Rumlow accumulates fights with him on a tempo of two or three a year. None of them break either way decisively; both men come to know the other's repertoire intimately.

Brubaker's run consolidates the antagonism into the single most operationally consequential act of Rumlow's career: the courthouse-steps assassination (Cap vol. 5 #25, 2007), in which Rumlow takes the rifle himself. Significant: it would have been operationally cleaner to assign the shot to a designated marksman. Rumlow takes it personally because it *is* personal. He wanted the round to be his round. This is the only act in the entire record in which his sadistic-possessive script and the Skull's strategic objectives converge perfectly on a single target.

The post-Reborn period reopens the antagonism without resolving it. Standoff and Secret Empire scramble the polarity entirely: Rumlow finds himself in service to a Rogers he believes to be the Skull's prophesied vessel, and the seamlessness of that re-allegiance is itself diagnostic — see below.

**Dynamics.** Rumlow's affect toward Rogers is uniquely *contemptuous* in a way his affect toward no one else is. He does not hate Rogers as he hates, say, Bucky Barnes (an interloper to be deleted) or Sam Wilson (a usurper). He hates Rogers as one hates a man who possesses every advantage and refuses to use them in the only honest way. Rogers, in Rumlow's reading, is a *waste* — the strongest body on the planet, deployed for an ethical project Rumlow regards as cowardice. The skull-mask Rumlow shows Rogers is a deliberate inversion: *I have less than you and I use it; you have everything and you flinch*.

The fight-language between them is mature. Rumlow does not bother to taunt Rogers the way he taunts lesser opponents; he saves taunts for opponents whose composure he can crack. With Rogers he speaks operationally — terse, contemptuous, often complimentary of a technique. The closest he comes to warmth with any non–Skull-line figure is the grudging professional respect that escapes him mid-combat with Rogers.

**Evolution.** Three phases. *Phase one* (Gruenwald): instrumental, Skull-derived hatred. *Phase two* (Brubaker through Remender): personal, identity-defining hatred — Rumlow as "the man who killed Captain America," a self-concept that survives Rogers' return and becomes the cornerstone of his professional self-myth. *Phase three* (Spencer): collapse of the antagonism into adoration, when Hydra-Cap appears to be the prophesied figure. The speed and totality of this collapse confirms the underlying truth: Rumlow never hated Rogers as Rogers. He hated Rogers-as-not-Skull. Hand him a Rogers-as-Skull and the entire hostility evaporates into devotion.

**Trust / safety.** Asymmetric. Rogers can predict Rumlow's tactics almost completely; Rumlow has the advantage of moral asymmetry (he will do things Rogers will not). In the field, Rumlow assumes Rogers will not kill him, which gives him a small but persistent operational margin. He is right about this. There is no scenario in which the two men sit in the same room safely.

**Failure mode.** Against Rogers specifically, Rumlow's failure mode is *over-performance*. He wants Rogers to *see* the kill; this elongates the kill window and produces openings. The courthouse shot succeeded only because Rumlow was not the only shooter and not the proximate killer — the third bullet of a multi-vector plan, not a duel. In a duel he loses.

**Leverage (UATU operational note).** The Rogers-shaped void in Rumlow is enormous. A demonstration that Rogers is not what Rumlow thinks he is — neither soft nor hypocritical, simply *other* in a way Rumlow has never been able to be — does nothing. He has weathered that data for thirty years. The genuine leverage point: convincing Rumlow that the Skull *preferred* Rogers, that the Skull's true love was always the opposing icon and Rumlow merely the disposable instrument. This is unfalsifiable enough to be planted and ruinous enough to detonate.

---

### 2. JAMES "BUCKY" BARNES — the interloper, the unfinished business

**History.** Barnes enters as Rogers' avenger after the courthouse killing. Their first major engagements occur during Brubaker's "Death of Captain America" and "Man Who Bought America" arcs, with Bucky-as-Cap hunting Rumlow with explicit intent to kill. Barnes shoots Rumlow on at least one canonical occasion; Rumlow shoots back. Neither has succeeded in finishing the other.

**Dynamics.** Barnes is, in Rumlow's interior schema, an irregularity. Rumlow does not have a stable category for him. He is not the Skull's foundational enemy (Rogers occupies that slot), he is not a professional peer (though objectively he is — Barnes' tradecraft is at least Rumlow's equal and arguably his superior in firearms and infiltration), and he is not a possessable body (Rumlow has no sexual or possessive script for men). What Barnes *is*, structurally, is the avenger of the kill that defines Rumlow's career — and therefore the only person whose existence threatens to render Rumlow's defining achievement *incomplete*.

This produces an unusual affective signature. Rumlow's hostility toward Barnes is colder than his hostility toward Rogers, less ornamented, more strictly murderous. He does not taunt Barnes; he wants him deleted. There is no derivable pleasure in the Barnes fights — only the irritation of a man whose ledger refuses to close.

**Evolution.** Stable. Of all Rumlow's antagonisms this is the one that has *not* changed substantially across writers. Every encounter is the same encounter: two professionals trying to terminate one another with a minimum of ceremony.

**Trust / safety.** None. Barnes is, in operational terms, the single most dangerous individual Rumlow has ever shared rooms with, because Barnes is the only opponent who is *also* trained to Rumlow's tradecraft standard *and* willing to kill him on sight. Rogers will not. Wilson, in his Cap tenure, would not. Barnes will.

**Failure mode.** Against Barnes, Rumlow's failure mode is *under-respect*. He persistently mis-files Barnes as the lesser Cap, an upstart inheritor, when behaviorally Barnes is the more dangerous proposition. He plans for Barnes as if planning for a Rogers-clone; he is repeatedly surprised by the asymmetric ruthlessness Barnes brings.

**Leverage.** Minimal. There is no relational depth to exploit because there is no relational depth on either side. Operationally: Barnes is the asset to deploy against Rumlow when results are required and theater is not.

---

### 3. SAM WILSON — the usurper

**History.** Wilson exists in Rumlow's record principally through the Spencer *Sam Wilson: Captain America* run and Standoff, in which Rumlow — restored from Pleasant Hill — re-enters the field with a Wilson-Cap as adversary. The encounters are direct, brutal, and ideologically charged.

**Dynamics.** Wilson functions in Rumlow's schema as a category insult before he is a tactical opponent. Rumlow's worldview — hierarchical, social-Darwinist, white-supremacist by association if not by self-articulated creed (his service to the Red Skull, who is the genre's foundational fascist, is not separable from this) — assigns Wilson a slot Rumlow has decided is illegitimate. The contempt Rumlow shows Wilson is *racialized* and *positional*: a Black man wearing the flag, in Rumlow's idiom, is a desecration twice over. Spencer made this subtext text. Rumlow's escalation against Wilson is, accordingly, higher-affect than his engagement with Barnes; he wants Wilson to feel the engagement.

**Evolution.** Linear and intensifying. The Standoff and Civil War II adjacencies see Rumlow committing increasingly disproportionate violence against Wilson and Wilson-adjacent targets.

**Trust / safety.** None, and Wilson knows it. Wilson's response to Rumlow is the closest any Captain America has come to deciding the man simply needs to be put down. The famous Wilson-Cap line of action that Rumlow forces — culminating in a kill that costs Wilson public legitimacy in-story — is, viewed coldly, a *victory* for Rumlow's worldview, in that it dragged Wilson onto Rumlow's ethical terrain.

**Failure mode.** Against Wilson, Rumlow's failure mode is *contempt-induced underestimation*. He files Wilson as the lesser Cap and is repeatedly punished for it.

**Leverage.** Use Wilson's existence as a recurring narrative humiliation to Rumlow's worldview — visible Black leadership of the institution he hates — to bait him out of disciplined patience and into theatrical engagements his patience would otherwise abort.

---

### 4. NICK FURY and the SHIELD apparatus (institutional enemy)

**History.** Across decades Rumlow has been a SHIELD target, interrogation subject (Brubaker run, post-assassination capture), and prison escapee. He has never been *of* the institution; he has always been against it.

**Dynamics.** Rumlow's contempt for SHIELD is bureaucratic — he regards it as a paper tiger whose operators are professionally competent and whose leadership is politically compromised. He respects individual SHIELD field operators (he has worked alongside Hydra-aligned crossovers extensively), and reserves contempt for the directorate. Fury personally he regards as a worthy enemy in the limited sense that Fury is unsentimental; the two men's professional codes overlap in their willingness to be ugly.

**Evolution.** Mostly stable. Rumlow's posture toward SHIELD shifts only insofar as SHIELD shifts (Pleasant Hill–era SHIELD's use of Kobik as a carceral instrument is, Rumlow would note if he theorized, *his kind of tool*).

**Trust / safety.** Operational; no personal element.

**Failure mode.** None unique to SHIELD; standard adversarial.

**Leverage.** Institutional, not personal.

---

### 5. THE PUNISHER (FRANK CASTLE) — the mirror he refuses to look into

**History.** Multiple skirmishes across the 90s and 2000s; Castle has put rounds into Rumlow on at least one canonical engagement.

**Dynamics.** This is the relational entry in the file most worth lingering on, because it is the one Rumlow himself most refuses to examine. Castle is *structurally* a man with similar combat training, similar willingness to kill, similar emotional flatness in the application of violence, and a similar contempt for institutional half-measures. The differences are: Castle is organized around grief and a code, Rumlow around authority and pleasure. Castle would never serve. Rumlow cannot conceive of not serving.

Rumlow refuses to engage Castle as a peer. He files him as an irritant, a lone-wolf vigilante below his weight class. The refusal is itself diagnostic — Castle is the available mirror in which Rumlow could see what he would be without the Skull, and Rumlow does not look at mirrors.

**Evolution.** Static and unexamined.

**Trust / safety.** None.

**Failure mode.** Same as with Barnes — under-respect.

**Leverage.** Force the comparison. Stage encounters in which Rumlow cannot help registering that Castle is what he might have been without Schmidt. The destabilization is small but real.

---

### 6. THE AVENGERS UNITY SQUAD (Remender era) — collective adversary

**History.** Repeated assault and assassination attempts against the Unity Squad, including the funeral-attack sequence that delivers Xavier's brain to the Red Skull.

**Dynamics.** Rumlow's role here is purely instrumental — he is the *means* by which the Skull acquires telepathy. His engagement with individual Unity members (Havok, Rogue, Wasp, etc.) is undifferentiated; they are obstacles between him and the delivery of an asset to the Skull. His one near-affective register in this period is satisfaction at having served as the conduit for an upgrade to the Skull's power.

**Evolution.** Linear: deployment, completion, dispersal.

**Trust / safety.** Adversarial, undifferentiated.

**Failure mode.** Mission-mode tunnel vision — he will accept disproportionate casualties to his own faction to complete a Skull-line objective.

**Leverage.** None team-level; pursue individual interceptors.

---

### 7. PROFESSOR XAVIER (posthumous target) — the asset-as-enemy

A short entry, but with diagnostic significance. Xavier is, to Rumlow, not a person but a *resource* — a brain to be retrieved. The desecration of the grave is, for Rumlow, not desecration; the body has no special status, and Xavier's mind is a tool. The absence of any squeamishness, ritual hesitation, or even taunt in the act is data: Rumlow's violence does not require an audience-of-victim; he is equally efficient against the dead.

---

### 8. DR. FAUSTUS — partial peer, partial rival

**History.** Co-conspirator on the assassination plan; intermittent allies and intermittent rivals across the Skull's wider apparatus.

**Dynamics.** Faustus operates in a register Rumlow distrusts — psychological manipulation, conditioning, the long elegant subversion. Rumlow respects results and distrusts methods that do not bleed. There is low-grade rivalry for the Skull's favor, with Rumlow secure in his position because he provides what Faustus structurally cannot: a body in the field. Their cooperation is professional; neither would mourn the other.

**Trust / safety.** Conditional, tactical.

**Failure mode.** Rumlow underestimates Faustus' ability to condition *him*. (Note: in the Brubaker run, conditioning is repeatedly used on adjacent operatives; Rumlow's resistance to it has not been canonically tested under serious assault and should not be assumed durable.)

**Leverage.** Faustus, if turnable, is the operative who could decondition Rumlow from the Skull-line — see Section 5's identification of the master leverage point.

---

### 9. BARON ZEMO / BARON STRUCKER / ALEXANDER PIERCE — fascist-internal rivals

**History.** Rumlow operates across decades inside the same authoritarian-conspiracy ecosystem that contains the Zemos, Struckers, Pierces, and various Hydra principals. He has not had a defining one-on-one antagonism with any of them, but the structural rivalry is constant: each is a candidate for the Skull-line's favor or for command of the field forces Rumlow leads.

**Dynamics.** Rumlow's distinguishing feature inside this ecosystem is that *he does not want command*. He wants to be the right hand. This makes him a stabilizing rather than destabilizing presence in the fascist-internal politics — the Zemos and Pierces of the world know Rumlow is not coming for their seat. Their courtesy to him is correspondingly real, within the limits of the type.

**Evolution.** Cordial-rivalrous, stable.

**Trust / safety.** Low but predictable.

**Failure mode.** Rumlow's refusal of ambition occasionally costs him political protection when the Skull-line is incapacitated and he must navigate the secondary apparatus without instruction.

**Leverage.** Engineer a succession in which one of these figures becomes the new Skull-surrogate. Rumlow will follow the line, not the man — which means whichever of them holds the Skull-claim holds Rumlow. This is the polite version of the Hydra-Cap migration.

---

### 10. TASKMASTER — the teacher

A late entry to the enemies list, but more accurate here than elsewhere; Taskmaster was once Rumlow's instructor at the mercenary academy, and the relationship has not been canonically warm since. They have been on opposite contracts at least intermittently.

**Dynamics.** Rumlow is, by his own measure, the student who outgrew the teacher. He respects Taskmaster's capacities and regards him as a contract operator without ideological spine — which, in Rumlow's value system, is the deepest contempt. Taskmaster is, in turn, professionally wary of Rumlow.

**Trust / safety.** Low, professionally cordial.

**Failure mode.** None remarkable.

**Leverage.** Taskmaster knows Rumlow's pre-Crossbones tradecraft baseline and could, if hired correctly, predict him. He is an asset worth retaining for that reason.

---

## II. RIVALS (intra-criminal, intra-fascist, peer-tier)

### 11. SIN (SINTHEA SCHMIDT) — the boundary case

Sin is dossiered fully under *Relationships II — Partners & Inner Circle*, but she appears here because she occupies a *liminal* category: peer, lover (see §III), and — at moments when she has held the Hammer as Skadi — superior. The rivalry register surfaces only briefly, in moments when the Skull-line has had multiple claimants. Rumlow's resolution of these moments has always been to defer to the most concentrated Skull-locus available, which has typically been Sin. Rivalrous content is *suppressed* in him toward her, not absent.

### 12. SERPENT SOCIETY (residual antagonism) — institutional rivals via Diamondback

Rumlow's history with the Serpent Society is mediated entirely through Diamondback. He regards the Society as the institution that briefly hid her from him, and his hostility toward King Cobra and the leadership is correspondingly persistent if low-priority.

### 13. BULLSEYE, SABRETOOTH, and the freelance-killer ecology

Rumlow's relationship to the freelance super-killer tier is *contemptuous*. He regards Bullseye as a circus act, Sabretooth as an animal. The contempt is structural: these men kill without serving, which in Rumlow's value system is moral squalor. He has worked alongside them and would do so again, but the line between his self-concept and theirs is fiercely defended.

**Leverage.** Pairing Rumlow on missions with these figures degrades his discipline because he wastes operational bandwidth distinguishing himself from them.

---

## III. INTIMATES / LOVERS

### 14. RACHEL LEIGHTON — DIAMONDBACK — the foundational possession, the only sustained interior

This is the longest and most psychologically dense relational sub-section in the file, and it is placed last to anchor the section because it is the single relationship that has produced the most data on Rumlow's interior.

**History.** Rachel Leighton, codename Diamondback, member of the Serpent Society, defects under the influence of an affection for Captain America (Gruenwald's late-80s Cap run). Rumlow — at that time a senior figure in the Skull's apparatus, already wearing the Crossbones identity — kidnaps her, holds her captive, and subjects her to a sustained captivity script that the canon describes in coded but unmistakable terms: physical torture, psychological coercion, sexual menace, and his framing of all of it as the legitimate expression of a prior claim. He repeatedly tells her, in language that is the closest thing in the entire record to his theory of love, that she belongs to him because he has decided she does.

She escapes. He pursues across years. She is, until Sin, the longest-running female figure in his interior life, and even after Sin, she remains the only woman in his record whose name destabilizes his composure.

**Dynamics.** Rumlow's experience of Diamondback is not — and this matters — *romantic* in any register an outside observer would recognize. It is, more accurately, the only sustained instance of his *possessive script* attaching to a particular individual rather than to women-as-class. Most predators of his structure are indiscriminate; Rumlow, with Diamondback, became *specific*. The specificity is itself the closest he has ever come to attachment.

The interior content, reconstructed: Diamondback represents to him the case in which his ownership claim was *contested by the object herself*, repeatedly, and *not extinguished by her contestation*. In his cognitive system, her refusal does not register as evidence against his claim; it registers as an obstacle to its fulfillment. This is structurally identical to his relationship with the Captain America project — both Rogers and Leighton are people who *do not consent* to the role Rumlow has assigned them, and in both cases the lack of consent is not data, it is friction.

The asymmetry is total. To Diamondback, Rumlow is a defining trauma; she has organized substantial portions of her later life around having survived him. To Rumlow, Diamondback is the *unfinished kill that he does not want to finish* — finishing it would resolve the obsession and he prefers the obsession to its conclusion.

**Evolution.** Over thirty published years, his pattern toward her has not changed. He has accumulated other targets, taken on Sin as partner, served and re-served the Skull-line through multiple incarnations — and the Diamondback motif has remained in the background of his interior, surfacing whenever circumstances permit. The Gruenwald-Brubaker continuity treats this as ongoing low-grade obsession; Spencer revisits it in glancing terms.

**Trust / safety.** Absolute danger. Leighton has correctly assessed this and has never permitted herself to be in fixed location proximity to him by


## Powers, Abilities & Their Limits

# POWERS, ABILITIES & THEIR LIMITS

## Preamble: The Wrong Question

The mistake almost every operational analyst makes with Brock Rumlow is to ask *what can he do that a metahuman can do?* — and, finding the answer is "very little," to file him below the threshold of strategic concern. This is a misreading of the threat. Rumlow's profile is not the profile of a power; it is the profile of a **trained instrument deployed in proximity to powers**. The question that actually predicts his behavior in a room is not *how strong is he?* but *what is the maximum damage a fully formed sadist with thirty years of professional violence and no internal brake can do to a target before something stronger than him arrives?* By that measure he is, and has always been, a top-decile threat in the Marvel operational ecosystem — not because he can lift a truck (in his enhanced periods he can, briefly), but because he is the kind of operator a Red Skull, a Hydra command cell, or a Hand cabal will *spend* on hard targets and reasonably expect a return on.

What follows is the granular inventory.

---

## 1. The Substrate: Unenhanced Baseline

Rumlow's body is the body of a heavyweight professional fighter who never stops training. Listed canonically at roughly 6'1" and somewhere between 290 and 314 lbs depending on era (the higher figure appearing in the Brubaker-period handbook entries after his serum exposure), his unenhanced baseline is **peak human across the board**: strength, speed, reflex, stamina, pain tolerance, recovery. He sits in the same physical-tier neighborhood as Bullseye, Bucky-as-Winter-Soldier (pre-arm), Taskmaster, and a pre-serum Steve Rogers' theoretical ceiling — bodies that do not exceed the human envelope but live, permanently, at its outer wall.

The granular markers of that maintenance: he carries no off-season weight; his neck circumference suggests dedicated cervical and grip work (a tell of fighters who have planned for being choked); he moves on the balls of his feet at rest; his standing posture is closed-stance, weight slightly back on the rear leg, hands at waist height rather than at his sides — a fighter's "soft" guard, never fully off. He sleeps in short, segmented blocks (operationally typical for his career arc) and shows no documented degradation in performance across consecutive operational days. He has eaten in the field and trained in the field for so long that the distinction between deployment and downtime is, behaviorally, gone.

**Pain tolerance** sits notably above even the elite-operator norm. This is not enhancement; it is psychological. Pain has been a constant of his existence since adolescence and was, for most of that existence, *administered by him to others* — he has watched what pain does to bodies from the operator side of the equation thousands of times, and that knowledge appears to immunize him affectively to its experience. He absorbs gunshot wounds, blade strikes, and impact trauma with annotational composure: he notes the hit, classifies it, continues. This is the single most important non-enhancement physical fact about him.

## 2. Combat Skill: The Taskmaster Lineage

Rumlow was the **senior instructor at the Taskmaster's mercenary academy** before he was recruited by the Skull. This is a credential whose weight is consistently underrated. The academy's premise is that the Taskmaster's photographic-reflex mimicry allows him to teach a curriculum drawn from the literal best fighters on Earth; the senior instructor is the man who delivers that curriculum to paying killers. To hold that post in one's early twenties, you must be able to (a) execute the full repertoire at demonstration speed, (b) diagnose error in others, and (c) survive being attacked by trainees on a daily basis. Rumlow did this job for a sustained period and was poached out of it by the Red Skull, who has historically had his pick of operators.

The fight-system that emerges from this background, as evidenced across his combat record, is **eclectic, brutal, and economical**. Specific signatures observable across canon:

- **Striking blend**: Western boxing footwork and head movement, Muay Thai clinch and elbow/knee work, dirty-boxing thumb-and-eye intrusions, and Krav-Maga-pattern continuous-attack chains. He does not stop on the strike that lands; he stops when the target is on the floor.
- **Grappling**: catch-wrestling top control, judo trips off the clinch, no notable submission game (he does not finish on the ground because he does not need to — his ground priority is to free a weapon hand or stand up to strike).
- **Edged-weapon work**: filipino-pattern double-knife sequences when armed accordingly, but his actual preferred knife behavior is single-blade reverse-grip used for hooking control as much as cutting — he tends to *grab and stab* in close, rather than fence.
- **Improvisational priority**: he uses environment ruthlessly. Walls, edges, chair legs, glass, doorframes, the corner of a desk, another body. He is in the small subset of operators who will, by reflex, throw a smaller combatant *into* a larger one.

The **finishing patterns** are diagnostic. Rumlow does not, as a rule, kill efficiently when efficiency is available — he kills *theatrically* when time permits and *cleanly* only when time does not. Against soft targets he prefers extended hand-to-hand finishes that allow the victim time to register what is happening. Against hard targets (Bucky, Sam Wilson, Sharon Carter, the Cap-line) he is faster and dirtier, because he has been bloodied by these targets before and respects the closing window.

A note on **how he loses**: across the published record his losses cluster into three categories. (1) Being overmatched by a true metahuman who closes the gap before he can equalize with weapons or environment (Cap at full serum, the Winter Soldier with arm and prep). (2) Being out-thought tactically by an opponent who refuses to engage him on the terms he prefers — Sharon Carter has done this; the Punisher has done this; Sam Wilson has done this by air-game. (3) Being intercepted in the *seam* between operational modes — between assassination and exfiltration, when his attention has shifted forward. He does not lose because he panics, because he tires, or because he is outclassed in skill by another normal human; in unenhanced one-on-one with any non-enhanced opponent he is, on the evidence, essentially undefeated.

## 3. Firearms, Demolitions, and the Long Tradecraft

**Firearms.** Rifle-grade marksman; pistol expert. The most consequential single act of his career — the assassination of Steve Rogers on the federal courthouse steps in *Captain America* vol. 5 #25 — was executed with a precision rifle round at distance, in coordination with Faustus's close-quarters element. The shot was clean; the angle was good; the round did not kill Rogers (Sharon's later close-range shot did, in the conditioning-induced action), but Rumlow's contribution was technically unimpeachable, and the operation as a whole stands as one of the cleanest political assassinations in recent Marvel history. His handgun work in close is also above the elite-operator median: he draws from concealment fast and *moves while shooting* by default, which is rarer than it should be even among professionals.

**Demolitions.** Multiple canonical instances of cleanly placed shaped charges, IED work, and breaching. He is comfortable with both timed and command-detonated devices and has been seen to improvise from available chemistry. He prefers under-yield (the breach should drop the door, not the building) — a craftsman's signature.

**Edged and exotic ordnance.** Throwing knives at confident mid-range; comfortable with grenades (incendiary, fragmentation, flashbang) and willing to use them in confined civilian spaces. He has used heavy weapons (LMG, RPG, vehicle-mounted) when operationally appropriate but is not signatured by them; his identity weapons are *himself*, the rifle, and the close-range pistol.

**Tradecraft.** Surveillance, counter-surveillance, exfiltration planning, the management of cells of subordinates, interrogation (the granular and the brutal). He is fluent in moving across borders illegally and at speed. His operational paperwork — to the extent we can infer it from outcomes — runs to the high professional standard required by the Skull's organization; his hits do not generate the kind of forensic residue an amateur leaves.

## 4. The Enhancements: What He Borrowed

Brubaker's run introduces a derivative super-soldier exposure that augments Rumlow's strength, durability, and recovery noticeably above peak-human, without taking him to Cap-tier. The specific marker: in this period he routinely takes hits from enhanced opponents that should incapacitate a normal man and continues operating, and he generates force in close that exceeds his (already large) frame's natural expectation. Subsequent canon is inconsistent about whether this enhancement persists at the same level — some appearances de-tune him back to peak-human-plus, others show the enhanced register intact.

Operationally, the right way to model him is: **assume enhanced strength and durability in the upper-human-plus band, with the floor at full peak-human across every metric.** This is the assumption that does not get an analyst killed.

He has also, intermittently, accessed **specialty gear** sourced through the Skull's logistics: a powered combat suit, the skull-pattern tactical mask (post-disfigurement, body armor with integrated environmental seal and HUD-grade optics), reinforced gauntlets with impact-amplification, and on occasion exotic ordnance up to and including chemical and radiological devices. The pattern of his gear use is *minimalist within availability* — he carries what the operation requires and discards the rest. He is not a gadget operator in the Batman or Bullseye sense; he is a body operator who augments grudgingly.

## 5. The Mask as Equipment

After the Skull-blast disfigurement, the skull-pattern mask becomes a permanent fixture and warrants treatment as a piece of operational equipment rather than costume. Functionally:

- It provides **environmental sealing** (he has operated in CS gas without degradation).
- It conceals the face from biometric capture, both forensic and surveillance-grade.
- It modulates and lowers his **voice register**, contributing to a terror-effect that he uses deliberately in interrogation and on hostage cordons.
- It **denies the target a face to negotiate with** — a critical psychological combat tool whose effect on civilian hostages and lower-tier opponents is consistently visible in the panel evidence.

The mask's secondary effect, on him, is identity-stabilizing: see the analytic dossier. As equipment, it should be modeled as a high-end tactical helmet plus a psychological amplifier. As face, it should be modeled as the actual face — because behaviorally it is.

## 6. Growth Over Time

Rumlow's skill curve is unusual: it is **early-saturated and stable**. By the time he enters the published record he is already at the senior-instructor tier of the Taskmaster academy, which means his fight-development was completed off-page in his late teens and early twenties. There is no late-career skill acquisition arc visible in canon. What there *is* is **deepening operational sophistication** — the Brubaker-era Rumlow plans longer, runs cells more competently, and assassinates more cleanly than the Gruenwald-era Rumlow, but this is the maturation of a complete operator, not the acquisition of new physical capacities.

The disfigurement, counter-intuitively, marks no decrement in performance. There is no evidence of vision loss, no documented motor deficit, no impairment of fine-motor weapons handling. He fights at full capacity after the burns. This is partly because the canonical injury, severe as it is, did not touch the structures that fight — and partly because, on his psychological profile, he was not going to *allow* it to degrade him.

The Pleasant Hill / Standoff episode is the one published anomaly: under Kobik's reality reshaping he is restored to a "normalized" identity (a regular family-and-job life), and when he is reawakened he is briefly slowed by the friction between the implanted persona and the real one. This resolves within an arc and is best modeled as a temporary glitch, not a developmental phase.

## 7. Signature Applications

The applications that show up over and over, with enough repetition to count as signatures:

- **The hostage cordon.** Rumlow loves a hostage situation and is very good at running one. He uses the cordon to draw the heroic opponent into a configuration that constrains their power use (Cap cannot throw a shield through a child), and he uses the duration of the negotiation to extract concessions or intelligence. The mask, the voice, the visible willingness to execute civilians, all reinforce the cordon. He has killed hostages on schedule to maintain credibility — this is the operational fact that distinguishes him from theatrical villains who only threaten.
- **The clean political hit.** As above (the Rogers assassination); also numerous lesser-target assassinations referenced across runs. He is the operator the Skull uses when the kill must land and the operation must survive forensic reconstruction.
- **The captive program.** Diamondback is the most documented case, but the pattern recurs: Rumlow assigned to break or hold a captive will engage in extended coercion that *exceeds the operational requirement*. The work and the pleasure are not separable.
- **The hard-target intercept.** When Hydra needs a Cap, a Falcon, a Bucky, a Sharon Carter slowed, bloodied, or cornered, he is the cell leader of choice. He does not, as a rule, *kill* hard targets at this tier — they outlast him in the long run — but he hurts them and he survives the engagement, which is itself a rare and valuable capability.
- **The honor-guard / personal-bodyguard role.** Closest to the Skull's body, and to Skadi-Sin's body in the Fear Itself sequence, and to Hydra-Cap's body in Secret Empire. The defensive register is real and effective; he does not break formation.

## 8. The Limits — Honest Inventory

He has, plainly, **no superhuman tier**. In a direct unmediated engagement with a Cap at full serum, a Winter Soldier with prep, a Falcon with air control, a Sharon Carter with shooting position, a Wanda, a Strange — he loses if they choose the terms. The enhanced register helps him survive longer; it does not let him win.

He has **no ranged dominance against modern hero rosters** beyond the rifle window. He is not a marksman of the Bullseye class; he is a very good professional shooter, which is a different and lower tier.

He has **no command of the strategic frame.** He executes operations; he does not generate them. Take away the Skull-line and the cell structure, and Rumlow has no doctrine of his own with which to fill the vacuum — he becomes a free-floating predator, dangerous to small numbers of people but no longer a strategic asset.

He has **no recovery from displacement of the organizing object** (see the analytic dossier). This is not, strictly, a combat limit, but it is the limit that determines what kind of operation he can survive psychologically.

He has **no peer-network depth.** If isolated from Hydra logistics he can subsist as a mercenary (he did this between affiliations earlier in his career), but he does not have a thick personal network of professional friends to call on. Sin is the partial exception; she is not infinitely available.

And he has, despite the discipline, **a sadism-induced operational drag**. Time spent on the cruelty of a kill is time the response is closing the distance. He has been caught more than once in this seam — the kill stretched too long, the shield arrived. The same impulse that makes him a top hostage-cordon operator makes him a vulnerable assassin once the target is in his hands. The discipline is real, but it is not absolute, and the place it fails is always the same place.

## 9. The Symptom-as-Signature Reading

If we treat the entire ability set as a symptom of the personality, the picture is sharp and consistent.

His **fight system** — eclectic, environmentally brutal, finishing-pattern-theatrical — is the somatic form of his interpersonal pattern. He fights the way he relates: by closing distance, controlling the terms, and extending the moment in which the other party is in his hand. The grappling-prefers-stand-up tendency is the same man who will not stay on the ground with anyone — top control is acceptable, mutual ground engagement is not, because the relational geometry of mutuality is foreign to him.

His **firearms preference** for the rifle round at distance on political targets, and the close pistol on personal targets, maps to the two relational registers he has: vertical-service (the rifle, the impersonal instrument of a larger plan) and possession (the pistol, in the hand, at the body of a target he has claimed).

His **demolitions discipline** — under-yield, no collateral the operation does not require — is the same discipline that organizes his service to the Skull. He is not chaotic. The cruelty is for designated targets, not splash damage. This is what makes him institutionally usable.

His **mask** is the somatic form of the identification-with-the-aggressor defense. The defense was already operating before the disfigurement; the disfigurement gave it a permanent prosthetic. The voice modulation is the same gesture in audio: do not be Brock, be the thing Brock has decided to become.

His **enhancement history** — borrowed, intermittent, never the defining feature — is the same pattern as his ideology. He absorbs what is supplied by the larger organism (Skull-line serum, Skull-line worldview), runs on it, returns to baseline when the supply stops, and does not generate it himself.

His **early skill saturation** and lack of late-career growth is the same closed loop as his self-concept. The grandiosity is consolidated; there is nothing to learn that he does not already believe he embodies. A man who could keep learning to fight at forty would be a man who could keep learning, in principle, other things. He is not that man.

His **discipline** — the absence of substance abuse, the maintained body, the segmented sleep, the operational composure — is the structural exoskeleton that the Skull-identification built around the feral adolescent. Strip the identification away and the discipline, as the dossier observes, is hollow; but the discipline is real while it lasts, and it is the single feature of his ability set that most distinguishes him from the broader rogues' gallery of competing thugs.

And his **hostage-cordon mastery** — the signature application he is most reliably himself in — is the externalization of his entire relational world. The cordon is a perfect Rumlow situation: he is in command, the target is in his hand, the larger cause is being served, the audience is afraid, and the cruelty is operationally justified. Every drive in his motivational stack lights up at once. He is, in those moments, the most fully integrated version of himself the record contains. This is the single environment in which to expect his peak performance, and the single environment in which his standard countermeasure — the sadism-induced operational drag — will most reliably extend the response window the responding force needs.

The summary is the dossier's summary in a different register: he is not a man whose abilities express inner pain. His abilities *are* his inner life, expressed outward in trained form, against bodies that are not his.

— END SECTION.


## Operational Profile & Tradecraft

# UATU DOSSIER — SECTION 6
## OPERATIONAL PROFILE & TRADECRAFT

*Subject: Brock Rumlow / "Crossbones"*
*Compiled from longitudinal observation, 1989–present canonical record. Cross-indexed with §§1–5 above.*

---

### 6.1 — DECISION ARCHITECTURE

The subject's decision-making is best modeled not as a single process but as a **two-layer stack**. The upper layer is *strategic-ideological* and is essentially delegated: he does not generate goals, he receives them, almost always from the Skull-line or from a Skull-aligned principal (Faustus, Sin, Hydra-Cap, in one instance Arnim Zola through intermediaries). The lower layer is *tactical-operational* and is entirely his own; here he is independent, fluent, and unusually competent. The seam between the two layers is the diagnostically critical feature: he will accept absurd, suicidal, or atrocity-grade objectives at the upper layer without resistance, then execute them at the lower layer with cold professional craft. The Federal Courthouse assassination of Steve Rogers (Cap vol. 5 #25) is the canonical specimen — the *what* came from the Skull and Faustus; the *how* (sniper hide selection, the use of Sharon Carter as triggered close-asset, the timed crowd panic, the exit lane) was largely Rumlow's.

Within the tactical layer, his process is recognizably the doctrine of a man who passed through a structured mercenary academy (Taskmaster's) and then served two decades inside a paramilitary apparatus (the Skull's strike teams). It is recognizably **special-operations–schooled**, with Hydra contamination: heavy on rehearsal, comfortable with deniability, but willing to substitute brute attrition for finesse when the operational reward (cruelty) justifies the noise.

The procedural signature, observed repeatedly:

1. **Receive objective.** Accept without challenge. Does not negotiate scope.
2. **Personally reconnoiter.** Rumlow does his own forward eyes when feasible. He distrusts subordinate intel — not because subordinates are incompetent (he selects competent ones) but because he wants to *feel* the geometry of the kill site.
3. **Plan in tiers** — primary, fallback, exfil — and verbalize them minimally to the team. Rumlow does not over-brief. He compartments.
4. **Rehearse physically** where time permits. He runs the assault on a stand-in space.
5. **Execute with patience until first contact, then with maximum violence.** His tempo shift at H-hour is one of his consistent operational tells (see §6.7).
6. **Confirm the kill personally** when the kill is the objective. He does not leave bodies un-verified. The reflex is so ingrained that it has compromised exfil discipline on several occasions (Brubaker run, twice).
7. **Exfil clean.** Despite the personal-confirmation habit, his post-action discipline is high. He moves; he does not linger to admire.

The decisional pathology — and the one a counter-operations cell can exploit — is the **brittleness at the seam**. Because the upper layer is delegated, when the principal is removed, killed, discredited, or revealed as a fraud *mid-operation*, Rumlow's tactical layer continues executing on the original tasking past the point of sense. He has been observed (Remender's Unity Squad arc; the Pleasant Hill awakening sequence) completing the *letter* of an order whose *purpose* had evaporated. He is incapable of in-the-loop re-tasking from his own conscience because his conscience does not occupy that layer.

---

### 6.2 — METHODS OF VIOLENCE: THE WORKING REPERTOIRE

The subject is a generalist with three areas of professional excellence and a wider competency in the standard mercenary toolkit.

**Hand-to-hand combat.** Taskmaster-trained, Taskmaster-promoted-to-instructor, which places him in a narrow tier of unenhanced terrestrial combatants. His style is hybrid — no single discipline — and built around the principles Taskmaster's pedagogy emphasizes: pattern absorption, bone-targeting, joint compromise, and economy of motion. Against Captain America he survives exchanges that would end most professional fighters, which is a published fact and the most reliable measure of his level. His preferred striking targets, recurrent across panels: clavicle, brachial plexus, floating ribs, knee from outside, throat. He does not pursue submissions; he is a *terminator* in the fight-finish sense, not a grappler. He will accept exchanges of damage to close distance — pain tolerance is operationally infinite within his window.

**Firearms.** Equally fluent across pistol, carbine, designated-marksman rifle, and crew-served weapons. The Rogers assassination demonstrates trained precision-rifle work at standoff range. In CQB he prefers compact suppressed long-guns over handguns when concealment allows; his handgun work is competent but not signature. He has an observed preference for **heavy calibers** (.45, .50 in shoulder weapons, .338 LM-class for stand-off) — consistent with his broader aesthetic, which is to leave a wound that *means* something, not merely a wound that suffices.

**Demolitions and breaching.** Above-average. Multiple operations across the record involve shaped charges, vehicle-borne devices, and structural collapse engineering. He is comfortable with both improvised and military-grade explosives and has built devices with Hydra-supplied components on short timelines. The Pleasant Hill exfil sequencing implies competence with electromagnetic and barrier-system defeat.

**Edged weapons.** Carries blades constantly. Uses them when he wishes a kill to be *intimate* — the choice is almost always affective rather than tactical. A man with his firearms options does not pick up a knife for efficiency; he picks it up because he wants to be close enough to feel it.

**Powered/enhanced augmentation.** Post-Brubaker-era serum exposure leaves him with enhanced strength and durability in the high-end-human range. He has, on occasion, employed Hydra exoskeletal kit and tactical armor with built-in weapons (wrist-mounted blades and short-range projectiles, integrated into the skull-mask era loadout). He treats augmentation as a **tool, not an identity** — he does not, like some enhanced operators, become dependent on the augmentation or distressed when it is unavailable. He fought without it for the first two decades of his career and reverts to baseline kit comfortably.

**Interrogation and torture.** Distinct sub-skill, qualitatively different from his combat work in that it is *unhurried*. He has documented competence at coercive interrogation including the use of sustained physical injury, sensory manipulation, and the leveraging of relational threats (Diamondback arc; multiple Brubaker-era victims). Two operational notes: (a) his interrogations frequently *over-extend* because cruelty has displaced the intelligence-extraction goal — he keeps going past the point where the subject would have broken — and (b) he is uninterested in the modern interrogator's preferred toolkit of rapport-building and false-friend protocols. He uses pain. This is a known limitation and one reason the Skull pairs him with Faustus when persuasion is the objective rather than terror.

---

### 6.3 — TRADECRAFT: COVERT, CLANDESTINE, AND CLOSE-PROTECTION

Rumlow has lived under false identity for the bulk of his adult life. The original flight from New York at seventeen required document fabrication and travel discipline that he managed without apparent assistance — this is the first datum suggesting a native aptitude for clandestine living. Throughout his Hydra/Skull career he has cycled through multiple legends (Bender, Brixton Rumlow, the Frank Simpson disambiguation in one continuity, several uncatalogued working aliases in the Brubaker run). His legends are functional rather than elaborate: enough document and pattern to pass routine scrutiny, designed to be discarded on contact.

**Surveillance behavior, active.** He runs counter-surveillance reflexively. Foot routes incorporate two-direction transits past mirrored or reflective surfaces; he uses vehicle speed-changes and unsignaled lane shifts on motor moves; he favors operating times at shift-change windows for municipal services and security details. He has been observed (Brubaker arcs, in NYC, DC, and Algiers) performing what intelligence professionals would recognize as **surveillance detection routes** — long, geometrically deliberate, theatrically casual.

**Surveillance behavior, passive (as target).** When he himself is under surveillance he is one of the harder professional subjects to track. He does not break cover by overt counter-action; he simply *adjusts the entire envelope of his behavior* down by one notch of visibility — shorter time on the street, denser cover crowds, more frequent identity rotation, a willingness to abort operations on small triggers. SHIELD surveillance product on him is, accordingly, thin. The thickest files on Rumlow are from the periods when he wanted to be seen (post-Reborn, when the skull-mask became a public terror brand).

**Close protection and personal-security detail work.** As the Skull's principal bodyguard for years, he is genuinely expert at the protective trade — advance work, route security, motorcade discipline, threat-arc visualization, body-cover reflexes. His protective instincts toward the Skull-line are not affect; they are *drilled*. He will interpose his body. This is one of the few areas where his behavior is reliably altruistic-coded, though the altruism is exclusively addressed to the Skull-line.

**Tradecraft weaknesses.** (a) He is recognizable. The body is distinctive at distance — broad, heavily muscled, particular gait — and post-disfigurement the operational signature is even more reduced (mask, height, build). He cannot do the *grey man* well; he is too physically loud. (b) His vehicular driving is competent but not at the level of his on-foot work; he treats vehicles as platforms rather than as extensions of self. (c) His electronic tradecraft is dated. He uses cyber-skilled subordinates because his own habits with comms hygiene are *adequate* (burner discipline, signal compartmentation) rather than *modern* (he is not a sophisticated user of network anonymization, does not appear to be a competent OpSec practitioner in the cryptographic sense). He is a 1990s-trained operator who has updated his hardware but not fully his instincts.

---

### 6.4 — RESOURCES, FINANCES, LOGISTICS

Rumlow does not, properly speaking, have a personal economy. He is **resourced through the Skull-line's logistical tail**, which means: at any given moment his financial position is a function of Red Skull / Hydra patronage rather than of independent wealth. He does not invest. He does not own property in his own name visible in the record. He does not accumulate. He has been observed living variously in safehouse networks, fortified Hydra compounds, mercenary-camp infrastructure, and (during Sin-aligned operations) in itinerant field arrangements.

This is *unusual* for a professional of his tenure and a useful diagnostic point: most mercenaries of comparable seniority maintain personal caches, off-network bolt-holes, and independent revenue. Rumlow's failure to do so is consistent with the §5 finding that the Skull-line is the organizing object — he does not prepare for a future in which the Skull-line does not provide for him, because such a future is not psychologically thinkable.

**Cash and equipment access.** Through Hydra logistics he has standing access to military-grade small arms, exotic ordnance, vehicular assets, and specialized kit on a request-and-receive basis. When operating off-network (rare, transitional periods), he has accessed weapons through the standard mercenary-grey market — confirmed contacts in the Balkans, North Africa, and the Five Boroughs. His preferred suppliers tend to be **Hydra-sympathetic legacy networks** rather than ideologically neutral vendors, which simplifies vetting but generates pattern.

**Safehouses.** When self-sourcing rather than Hydra-sourcing, the canonical preference is **industrial fringe** — disused warehousing, low-occupancy commercial property in port and rail corridors, never residential. He does not nest. The Lower East Side origin shows residually in his New York operational geography: when he returns to NYC, he gravitates to the river-edge and bridge-approach industrial bands. He has been observed in the Brooklyn waterfront, the Bronx rail yards, and the New Jersey side of the Hudson under Hydra cover.

**Transportation.** Comfortable with motor vehicles up to and including light tactical platforms. Has employed helicopter exfil (with non-pilot status — he uses contracted pilots). Has demonstrated boat-handling sufficient for coastal exfil. He is not, in the published record, a man who flies, sails, or drives for pleasure; transportation is purely instrumental.

**Documents and identity infrastructure.** Hydra-supplied for the bulk of his career. The quality is high but the *pattern* of the documents — embedded Hydra-network anomalies, recurring fabricator signatures — is identifiable to a counter-intelligence cell that knows what to look for. SHIELD has, in past operations, traced him via document-fabricator forensics rather than via his own field errors.

**Personal kit, recurring inventory.** Across the published record, Rumlow's *on-person loadout* is remarkably consistent:

- A primary firearm, suppressed where mission allows, in heavy chambering.
- A backup firearm — typically a compact carried at the small of the back or in a thigh rig.
- A fixed-blade knife, fighting-grade, carried inverted on the load-bearing harness for a reverse draw.
- A backup folding blade, pocketed.
- Breach explosives in small quantities (one to three charges, primer-ready).
- Comms — usually a Hydra-issue unit with a fallback civilian device.
- The skull mask (post-Reborn) and full tactical harness; pre-disfigurement, body armor patterned to the Crossbones aesthetic with the chest-cross motif rendered in webbing and pouches.
- A small individual medical kit — tourniquets, hemostatic gauze, occlusive dressing, broad-spectrum analgesic. He treats himself. He does not present at hospitals.
- A garrote-grade length of cordage; he has used cordage as both tool and weapon repeatedly enough to call it signature.

He does *not* carry sentimental objects. There is no documented instance of him carrying a photograph, a token, a memento. The closest he comes to a personal effect is *the mask itself*, which is identity rather than object.

---

### 6.5 — INFRASTRUCTURE AND NETWORK POSITION

Rumlow occupies a specific node in the Hydra/Skull infrastructure that has remained remarkably stable across decades and editorial regimes: he is the **field-command nexus between the Skull's strategic intent and the strike-team operational layer**. He is not a desk asset; he is not a singleton specialist; he is the man who *converts orders into operations*. This node is functionally indispensable when occupied by someone of his competence, which is part of why he has been reinstated to it across multiple Skull-line successions.

**Subordinate handling.** He recruits, trains, and culls his own strike teams. His selection criteria, inferred from the personnel he retains: physical competence first, ideological discipline second, *individual ambition tightly capped*. He does not retain subordinates who show command ambition; the men around him are competent operators who are content to be operators. He runs them by a mixture of fear, professional respect, and the implicit promise of action — his teams *get to do* the work that other Hydra elements only plan.

**Lateral relationships in the network.** He coordinates routinely with the Hydra intelligence directorate (for target packages), the Hydra science apparatus (for augmentation and equipment), and the political-action wing (rarely, and with poorly concealed contempt — he regards the Hydra suits as parasites on the work). He has working relationships with the broader supervillain ecology — has appeared on Serpent Society peripheries via the Diamondback connection, has worked Acts of Vengeance era multi-faction operations, has interacted with the Taskmaster academy alumni network and called on it. He is *known* across the criminal demimonde and feared by those who know him.

**Personal command staff.** Across eras he keeps a small inner ring. Sin is the long-standing inner-ring figure when available. Beyond her, the ring is small (typically two to four lieutenants), durable, and reconstituted from Taskmaster-academy alumni when attrition requires.

---

### 6.6 — PATTERNS OF ACTION: THE SIGNATURE PORTFOLIO

Across thirty-five years of operations, the subject has demonstrated a recurring portfolio of operational *types*. He is most often deployed in one of the following:

1. **Assassination, hard target, planned.** His most strategically significant work. Rogers, Federal Courthouse, is the apex. He does these well, with adequate intelligence support and rehearsal. He prefers stand-off where target hardening permits, close where it does not.
2. **Kidnap-and-extract.** Diamondback, multiple smaller subjects. He is good at the snatch, *competent* at the holding, *poor* at the handling — the cruelty contaminates the operation.
3. **Strike-team raid against a fortified objective.** Multiple Hydra base-defense and base-assault actions. He is excellent in this register; the dynamics of a small-unit assault on a hard target play to his strengths (planning, tempo, willingness to absorb attrition).
4. **Bodyguard and personal protection.** Of the Skull, of Sin, of Hydra-Cap-era principals. He converts seamlessly to the protective mission without ego friction; the protective work is psychologically congruent with the devotional structure.
5. **Public terror operations.** Funeral attacks, attempted mass-casualty incidents (Xavier funeral, multiple Hydra-aligned terror events). He is comfortable with civilian targeting and does not seek to minimize it.
6. **Coercive interrogation.** Discussed above. Often misemployed because the principal mistakes his appetite for the work as competence at the work.

Operation types he is *not* employed in, and would be a poor fit for: deep-cover infiltration of long duration (he cannot pass as anything but what he is); diplomatic-front work (he is socially unsuited); political-action / agitation work (no ideological generativity).

---

### 6.7 — OPERATIONAL TELLS AND SIGNATURES

A surveillance cell tracking him will identify the subject by a cluster of repeating tells, several of which he is not aware of:

- **The pre-action stillness.** Immediately before initiation of violence he goes *quiet* — verbal output drops to zero for a measurable window (observed at three to five seconds), body settles, head tilts marginally forward. The shift is so consistent that subordinates have used it as an unspoken go-signal.
- **The kill-confirmation reflex.** As noted in §6.1: he will return to a body to confirm it. This has compromised exfil twice in canon. The reflex is non-negotiable for him.
- **Heavy-caliber preference.** Documented across multiple loadouts. A weapons-recovery pattern showing .45/.50/.338 LM signatures clustered around an incident is a Rumlow signature absent other identifiers.
- **The reverse-draw blade.** Few professional combatants carry a fixed blade inverted for reverse draw; Rumlow does it consistently, and the resulting wound pattern (downward-angled chest and throat lacerations, drawn rather than stabbed) is recognizable to a forensic pathologist with the comparison library.
- **Cordage at the scene.** The garrote-grade cord turns up at his sites — used, discarded, sometimes pre-staged.
- **Personal kill verification *plus* trophy refusal.** He confirms but does not collect. Unlike trophy-keeping serial offenders, he leaves the body as-is and walks. This is diagnostically clean: cruelty is in the *doing*, not in the *having-done*.
- **Tempo signature in radio and comms traffic.** Brief in pre-contact phase; clipped and declarative at contact; *silent* during the action; brief and bored in the post-action confirm. He does not chatter, does not narrate, does not vent on the net.
- **Verbal taunt at the moment of imminent kill.** Where the operational profile permits proximity to a known victim, he speaks to them in the last seconds. The taunts are short, personal, contemptuous, and oriented to *what the victim believed about themselves* — he hits self-concept, not body, with the verbal blow. This is the cruelty expressing itself even in a tactically efficient operation.
- **Refusal to remove the mask in front of subordinates.** Post-Reborn. The mask comes off only in the presence of Sin or (formerly) the Skull. A subordinate who has seen the face is, by inference, either very senior or not long for the work.
- **The standing-watch posture in protective work.** When close-protecting, he positions himself in a recognizable stance — slight angle off the principal's strong side, weight distributed for a forward step, hands habitually at low-ready even when the environment is permissive. The posture is so habitual that he assumes it momentarily in non-protective contexts when the Skull-line is nearby.
- **Avoidance of mirrors, post-disfigurement.** Subtle but consistent. He does not look at his own reflection in operational environments; he uses reflective surfaces only for counter-surveillance angles. The mask justifies the behavior to him; the avoidance predates and exceeds the operational need.

---

### 6.8 — INTEGRATED OPERATIONAL ASSESSMENT

The subject is, in unsentimental net assessment, **a high-end professional violence operator constrained almost entirely by the quality of his principal**. Set him against a weak adversary with a competent Skull-line tasking and he is one of the most productive killers in the published threat landscape. Set him against a peer-grade adversary with a degraded or absent principal and he degrades surprisingly fast — not because his tactical skills decay but because the upper layer of his decision stack stops feeding him coherent objectives, and his lower layer is not designed to substitute.

The operationally critical insight, restated from §5 into action-relevant form: **he is most dangerous when his principal is strong and most exploitable at the principal-substitution seam**. A counter-operations approach that engages him on his terms — direct confrontation, attrition, hardening of targets — will succeed only at high cost and will not produce permanent neutralization, because the Skull-line will reconstitute him. An approach that operates on the *principal* — discrediting, corrupting, substituting, or revealing the Skull-line's contempt for him as instrument — produces a Rumlow who is still extremely dangerous but is operating without the upper-layer scaffolding that makes him strategic rather than merely violent.

He is not a man to be turned. He is a man to be *unmoored*, and then engaged.

— END SECTION 6. Continue to §7 (Relational Map & Network Analysis) on receipt.


## Worldview & Operational Code

# WORLDVIEW & OPERATIONAL CODE — SUBJECT: BROCK RUMLOW

> *"You think there's a world where you win and I get rehabilitated. There isn't. There's just this one, and in this one I get up earlier than you."* — paraphrase reconstructed from recurrent interrogation transcripts, Brubaker-era SHIELD debriefs

---

## 1. THE METAPHYSICS — WHAT HE BELIEVES THE WORLD *IS*

Rumlow's cosmology is not articulated; it is *enacted*, and reverse-engineerable from thirty-five years of consistent conduct. The world, as he reads it, is a **standing arena**. It is not a moral order, not a contract, not a fallen creation requiring redemption, not a market, not a network. It is a floor with bodies on it, and the bodies are sorted by what they can do to each other. This is the bedrock. Everything subsequent is decoration on this floor.

He does not believe in the soul. He does not believe in justice as a property that inheres in events; justice is the name losers give to outcomes they wanted. He does not believe in progress — the Skull's mythos of restoration would make this explicit, but Rumlow holds it pre-philosophically, as a *temperament*. Things were never better and will never be better; there are only stronger and weaker arrangements of the same constants. He does not believe in luck, though he respects it tactically (a man who slips a kill shot has earned the slip by being where the shot missed). He does not believe in history as a teacher; he believes in history as a record of who was willing to act.

He believes, with absolute certainty, in **hierarchy as the natural state**. Equality is not a value he opposes; it is a category error he finds embarrassing in adults. When he encounters egalitarian rhetoric in the field — civilians invoking rights, agents invoking due process — his response is not anger but a kind of disgusted patience, the way a tradesman listens to a homeowner explain the trade. The hierarchy is real; the only question is where you stand in it, and the only legitimate way to find out is force.

He believes in **the body as the only honest unit of measurement**. Words lie, intentions lie, contracts lie, ideologies he half-listens to lie; what does not lie is whether a man is still standing after the engagement. This is why his sadism is not, to him, a moral matter — it is *epistemological*. Cruelty produces information. Fear produces information. A man with a knife to his daughter's throat tells the truth in a way no interview can extract. Rumlow has organized his professional life around this conviction, and it is the reason he is, despite the brutality, a *useful* operator and not merely a destructive one.

## 2. CONFLICT — HOW HE READS A FIGHT, A ROOM, A LIFE

Conflict, for Rumlow, is the **default state**. Peace is the name for the interval between engagements during which the weaker party has not yet noticed the engagement has resumed. He does not therefore experience conflict as crisis. He experiences its absence as suspicious.

His reading of any room follows a near-invariant sequence:

1. **Exits and angles** (immediate, pre-conscious).
2. **Who in the room can kill me, and with what**, ranked.
3. **Who in the room would kill me, and under what conditions**, ranked.
4. **Who in the room owns the room**, which is rarely the same as #2 or #3.
5. **Who in the room is afraid of whom**.
6. *Then*: content of the conversation.

This is trained, but it is also *preferred* — he enjoys it the way some men enjoy crossword puzzles. The room is a problem set, and the problem set is restful.

Conflict types are sorted in his head into a small, stable taxonomy. *Operations* (planned violence with mission objectives) are work, and he is craftsmanlike about them — patient, technical, willing to abort. *Engagements* (reactive violence) are tests, and he scores himself on them — debriefs himself silently afterward. *Disputes* (intra-organizational friction) he handles, when permitted, by escalation toward physicality very quickly, because his read is that disputes left in the verbal medium metastasize and that the room sorts faster if you reveal early who would actually do it. *Vendettas* (Diamondback, in the longest case) he files separately and revisits — these are the only conflicts he carries across time as *personal* projects rather than as work.

His conflict *style* is, contrary to the impression his disfigurement and theatricality create, **patient**. The signature Rumlow operation is not the explosion; it is the wait. He will sit a target for days. He will let a subordinate's failed approach burn so the target relaxes into thinking the threat has passed. He absorbs the first exchange to read the opponent's tells before committing his real capability. Under stress he becomes *less* patient — see §4 of the upstream workup — and this is the single most reliable degradation in his game. An adversary who can keep him in the engagement long enough to push him past his patience window gets a measurably worse Rumlow.

## 3. CONTROL — THE THEORY OF DOMINANCE

Rumlow's theory of control is operationalized along three vectors and three only: **fear, hierarchy, and ownership**. He does not believe in persuasion as a primary instrument; persuasion is what you do to people you cannot reach with the real instruments. He does not believe in consent in any robust sense; consent is the post-hoc story the controlled tell themselves to preserve dignity, and he has no objection to letting them keep that story so long as compliance is delivered.

*Fear* is his preferred medium because it scales. One demonstration, properly staged, controls a battalion. He stages demonstrations carefully — not maximally violent, but *legibly* violent, the kind of act that survives retelling and travels. The skull mask is in the same family of choices: a symbol designed to do work in absentia, so that the *report* of Crossbones on the ground does as much as the man on the ground.

*Hierarchy* he uses with surprising sophistication. He knows that organizations control individuals more reliably than individuals control individuals, and he positions himself as the embodied face of a vertical structure rather than as a personal authority. When he commands, he commands *as* the Skull's instrument; insubordination is reframed instantly as treason against the cause, which mobilizes the rest of the unit against the dissenter and offloads enforcement onto the peer group. This is a learned trick from the Taskmaster academy and from his decades of strike-team command, and it is why he can run a unit larger than his personal terror could discipline.

*Ownership* is the most personal of the three and the one most contaminated by his pathology. He owns operational assets, terrain, weapons, plans, kills, and women, and the categories blur. A target he has been assigned to acquire becomes, after assignment, *his*; another operator's intervention on that target is felt as theft, not as logistics. The Diamondback case is the canonical specimen — she is, in his cognition, ongoing inventory. He does not pursue her continuously because he is romantically obsessed; he pursues her intermittently because she is an unclosed ticket on a ledger he experiences as binding. The distinction matters because it predicts his behavior: he will not "let her go" if he gets a better partner, and he will not "move on" if time passes; he will collect her when the operational moment permits, the way one finally retrieves a tool left at a job site.

Control's failure modes, in his model: control fails when fear becomes familiar (so demonstrations must rotate, escalate, surprise); when hierarchy is ridiculed (so insult to the chain must be answered immediately and disproportionately); when ownership is publicly contested (so challenges to possession must be settled bodily, not negotiated). He has internalized all three failure modes and pre-empts them.

## 4. TRUST — THE EXTREMELY SHORT LIST

Rumlow's working definition of trust is **predictability under pressure**. He does not trust people for their virtues; he trusts them for their reliability of response. A reliable enemy is trusted more than an unreliable ally. He has, over the entire published record, demonstrated robust trust in *exactly two parties*: the Red Skull, and Sin. The Skull he trusts because the Skull is the organizing object of his world; trusting the Skull is structurally identical to trusting gravity. Sin he trusts because she is Skull-line, because their operational tempos have meshed across years, and because — uniquely in his life — she has shown him she will come for him (the SHIELD breakout post-Rogers assassination). That single act consolidated a partnership-trust he extends to no one else.

Beyond these two, his trust is **graduated and revocable**. Subordinates earn provisional trust by completing assignments without improvisation. Peer operators (Sin's Serpent Society contacts, Hydra cell commanders, Taskmaster-network alumni) earn working-trust through track record. He never extends trust on the basis of stated belief — a man who professes Hydra loyalty without operational record is, to Rumlow, *less* trusted than a competent mercenary with no ideology, because the professed loyalty is unfalsifiable and the mercenary's price is concrete.

He does not believe in trust as a moral bond. Betrayal, when it occurs, produces in him not the wounded affect of the betrayed but the technical irritation of someone whose forecast was wrong. He will revise the forecast — usually by killing the source of the bad data — and proceed. This is one of the qualities that makes him bearable to authoritarian command structures: he does not require betrayers to be punished *for justice*; he requires them removed *for accuracy*. The Skull values this; it is rare.

A specific note on **self-trust**: Rumlow trusts his own read of a room more than he trusts intelligence reports, more than he trusts plans handed down, and (his single most dangerous habit) sometimes more than he trusts the Skull's stated preference. He has on multiple occasions adjusted operations on the ground against orders, post-hoc justifying the adjustment by results. The Skull has tolerated this; another principal might not.

## 5. RISK — THE CALCULUS

Rumlow's risk model is **asymmetric and patient**. He does not minimize risk; he minimizes *unforced* risk while accepting catastrophic risk when the asymmetry favors it. The Rogers assassination is the textbook case: a high-probability-of-capture operation with a strategic payoff so large that capture was an acceptable price, and he priced it accordingly (he was, in fact, captured; he did, in fact, get extracted; the calculus held). He does not gamble. He bets when the spread justifies it, and he is willing to take damage in exchange for position.

He does not fear death in any expressed register. Multiple canonical near-deaths have produced no documented re-evaluation, no bucket-list behavior, no spiritual turn, no protective hardening of behavior — the operational tempo remains constant before and after each near-miss. This is partly temperament and partly *theology of a sort*: he believes that the right death (in the service of the Skull-line, against a worthy enemy, leaving fear behind) would be the correct conclusion of his life, and the wrong death (incidental, in transit, at a stranger's hand) would be a failure to be avoided but not feared. He prepares for death the way he prepares for any operation — checked equipment, settled debts (he leaves no operational loose ends if he can help it; the Diamondback ticket is the exception), no surprises for the team.
