He will continue to take the most personally meaningful jobs — assassinations of Avengers-adjacent symbolic targets — himself rather than delegate, because the *meaning* of the kill matters to him in a way it doesn't to a pure professional. Expect at least one further attempt on a Rogers-line target (the mantle, not necessarily the man); his unfinished psychological business with Captain America is structural, not incidental, and any new Cap will reactivate it.

**Phase two (consolidation into handler/instructor, ~5–10 years).** Cumulative TBI burden, joint degradation, and the slowing of reflex will push him — without his consent — into a higher proportion of training and command work. This is where the Taskmaster-academy origin recurs as destiny: he began as an instructor of killers and will end as one. Expect a Hydra/Skull-line cadre school, formal or informal, with Rumlow as its operational dean. This is the role in which he is most dangerous to the long-term security environment, because he reproduces himself in pupils. The Gruenwald-era data point — that he was the senior instructor at Taskmaster's academy by his early twenties — is the load-bearing predictor here.

**Phase three (terminal sortie, indeterminate timing).** Rumlow will not die in bed. The structure of his psychology forecloses graceful exit; the moment he is no longer useful to the Skull-line in his preferred capacity, he will *engineer* a high-stakes operation to reassert his utility. This is the most predictable single behavioral event in his future: a late-career signature operation, undertaken at unfavorable odds, in which he attempts to deliver a strategic-level result (a head-of-state-grade assassination, a symbolic site attack, a coup-component) by hand. Probability that he dies in this sortie or its immediate aftermath: high. Probability that he attempts it: near-certain, conditional on his still being ambulatory and the Skull-line still existing to receive the offering.

---

## 9.3 The Fork Points — Where the Trajectory Could Bend

There are a finite number of events that could meaningfully alter the base-rate arc. Each is enumerated with the expected response.

### Fork A: Permanent Severance of the Skull-Line

The single most consequential possible disruption. Sin killed permanently, the Red Skull permanently expunged (not body-swapped, not Kobik-restored, *gone* in a manner Rumlow accepts as final), no plausible successor.

*Predicted response:* not grief in any normative sense, and emphatically not redemption. The clinical picture would be an **identity vertigo** — the organizing introject collapses and there is no second-tier scaffold. Likely behavioral outputs, in declining probability:

- Attempted vengeance campaign against whoever ended the line, pursued past tactical sense, terminating in his death. This is the highest-probability outcome (~55%). It is the path of least psychological reconstruction; he simply runs the existing program one final time without its object, like a dog who keeps fetching after the owner is gone.
- Attachment to a *substitute* authoritarian object: a surviving Hydra principal, a new fascist movement, a Zemo-line claimant. Probability ~25%. The substitution will be unstable because the Skull-line was not just an authority but a *bloodline mythology* he had braided into; replacements will feel synthetic and his service will be more brittle, more prone to humiliation-driven defection or sabotage.
- Withdrawal into mercenary work, unaligned, taking contracts for hire. Probability ~15%. This is the "professional decline" path. He would be more dangerous to individual targets and less dangerous to the strategic environment.
- Genuine psychological reorganization toward something other than predation. Probability <5%, and not zero only because the dossier must acknowledge the irreducible unpredictability of any human across decades. There is no evidentiary basis for this outcome; it is a courtesy probability.

### Fork B: Discovery That He Has Been Used and Discarded by the Skull-Line

Distinct from Fork A. The Skull-line exists and continues, but Rumlow learns — and *cannot disbelieve* — that he has been a disposable instrument, mocked privately, slated for replacement, or used as a sacrificial pawn in a plan he was not told about.

*Predicted response:* the most psychologically destabilizing scenario in the dossier. His defenses are all outward-facing; they have no architecture for processing betrayal from above. Likely outputs:

- A short window — days to weeks — of operational paralysis. He will continue to function physically but his tactical patience, the asset that makes him strategic-grade, will degrade. This is the window in which he is most catchable.
- Followed by one of two divergent paths: (i) *re-idealization* — he reconstructs the betrayal as a test or as a necessity of the cause, restoring the introject by force of will, returning to service. Probability ~50%, because identification with the aggressor is his deepest defense and it will fight to survive. (ii) *Schismatic violence* against the Skull-line itself, pursued with the same fanaticism formerly devoted to it. Probability ~35%. The remaining ~15% is some combination of breakdown, defection to a substitute, or self-destructive sortie.

Operationally: this fork is the highest-leverage intervention available to an adversary willing to invest in a slow informational operation. It does not require killing the Skull; it requires making the Skull's contempt for Rumlow legible to Rumlow in a form he cannot dismiss.

### Fork C: Sin Specifically

Sin's status is a separate variable from the Skull's, because the bond there has a different structure — partnership-coded, the closest thing to a peer in his life, and a transfer-object for the Skull's authority during periods of the Skull's absence. Sin killed in front of him, by an enemy he is denied the ability to reach, would produce the most overt affective rupture in his life. Sin *turning on him* — choosing another enforcer, dismissing him as obsolete, taking the Skull's contempt as her own — would activate Fork B's vertigo with additional sexual-possessive injury layered in. The Diamondback datum applies: women who slip his grasp become permanent organizing grievances; a Sin who slipped his grasp would be the grievance of his life.

### Fork D: A Second Disfiguring or Disabling Injury

He has absorbed one identity-grade injury and metabolized it into role consolidation. A second — loss of a limb, blinding, paralysis — would test whether the same mechanism scales. Best estimate: it does, up to a threshold. He could lose a hand and become a more theatrical version of himself; he could lose mobility and become a handler; he could not lose his cognition and remain himself. A TBI severe enough to compromise executive function would terminate him as an operator, and given that his entire psychic structure is built on operational efficacy, the most probable response to that loss is suicide-by-mission within the first window he can engineer.

### Fork E: Carceral Containment of Indefinite Duration

A genuine, escape-proof imprisonment — not a SHIELD black site he and Sin will exit in twelve issues, but something on the order of a Raft-grade or Pleasant-Hill-grade containment with no political will for release. *Predicted response:* he does not deteriorate the way isolated prisoners typically deteriorate. He does the time. He trains in the cell. He cultivates whatever guards or fellow prisoners he can. He waits, and his waiting is one of his core competencies. The Pleasant Hill sequence demonstrated that even *cognitive overwriting* of his identity is reversible by him on contact with the original organizing stimuli. Containment without identity-disruption simply preserves him; containment *with* identity-disruption produces only a delayed reactivation. The only carceral solution that holds him is one that permanently severs him from any future contact with the Skull-line — which loops back to Fork A.

### Fork F: Contact with Diamondback (Rachel Leighton) After Long Separation

The single relational variable with documented power to destabilize his affect. A forced or engineered encounter — particularly one in which she is operationally his superior, or in which she demonstrates indifference rather than fear — would not produce reform. It would produce a tactical error window. He cannot file her as past. She is the only person in his record whose existence implies a Brock Rumlow that the Crossbones identity does not fully cover, and contact reactivates the implication.

### Fork G: The Hydra-Cap Pattern Recurring

A future iteration of the *Captain America is secretly ours* gambit — whether literal repetition, a new mantle-holder corrupted, or a symbolic equivalent — is functionally guaranteed in the publication environment and will draw Rumlow in as gravitational matter. The Spencer-era data established that he does not require the leader to be the Skull; he requires the leader to be *the Skull's project*. This makes him reliably exploitable by any sufficiently sophisticated authoritarian operation that frames itself as Skull-aligned, even falsely. A skilled adversary could weaponize this — running a false Skull-project flag to draw him into a trap. He would be unusually credulous about such a flag because credulity-toward-the-cause is the very mechanism that organizes him.

---

## 9.4 Open Questions the Record Does Not Resolve

These are the gaps that would change the projection if they were filled.

**(i) The face under the mask, longitudinally.** The dossier records the absence of grief response to the disfigurement. What it cannot resolve is whether that absence is durable across the second and third decades post-injury. Most disfigurement patients have a long-tail affective course; Rumlow's defenses are atypical but not necessarily immortal. A future depressive episode, if it occurred, would be the first crack in the structure. Watch for: declining grooming under the mask, declining sexual activity, declining mission-volunteerism. None have been observed; their appearance would matter.

**(ii) The ceiling of his service capacity.** He has never been documented refusing a Skull-line order. We do not know if there is an order he would not execute. The likeliest candidate categories are (a) orders to kill Sin, (b) orders to unmask publicly as humiliation, (c) orders to *stop* — the order to stand down may be psychologically harder for him than the order to kill. Each is a useful probe for an adversary.

**(iii) Whether age produces ideological drift.** Authoritarian foot soldiers occasionally radicalize *past* their original cause in late career, becoming purer than their masters. Rumlow has shown no theorizing tendency, which argues against this, but the Spencer-era credulity suggests a residual capacity for true-belief intensification. If he begins generating ideology rather than absorbing it, the threat profile changes upward.

**(iv) The succession question.** If he runs a cadre school in phase two, who does he produce, and do any of them inherit his bond-pattern with the Skull-line rather than with him? A pupil who out-Rumlows Rumlow and is preferred by Sin or by a Skull-successor would activate Fork B by structural inevitability.

**(v) The unenhanced/enhanced question.** His exposures to serum derivatives have been intermittent. A sustained enhancement program in late career — Hydra investing in keeping its senior enforcer field-capable — would extend the operational phase by a decade or more and forestall the handler-transition. Conversely, the *withdrawal* of an enhancement on which he had come to rely would produce a humiliation-grade decline he would not tolerate quietly.

---

## 9.5 Growth Versus Catastrophe — The Asymmetry

A standard forward assessment offers symmetric pathways: here is what would push the subject toward integration; here is what would push them toward collapse. For Rumlow, the pathways are not symmetric, and the dossier should be honest about this.

**Toward catastrophe (well-mapped, multiply redundant):** any of Forks A, B, C, D-severe, or G-trap; the base-rate continuation curve terminating in the predicted late-career sortie; an environment that continues to reward his existing competencies (the most likely environment). Catastrophe in his case means *his* catastrophe and the catastrophe he authors before it — likely a multi-casualty terminal event, likely with symbolic targeting, likely while serving or attempting to serve the Skull-line.

**Toward growth (sparsely mapped, weakly supported):** the genuine pathways are narrow and require conditions that the record gives no evidence of obtaining.

- *Pathway 1: Catastrophic loss of the organizing object combined with prolonged carceral containment and an unusually skilled long-form therapeutic engagement, beginning at an age at which mortality has become subjectively real to him.* This is the Malcolm-X-grade reorganization pathway — the prison-as-crucible model — and it requires (a) the Skull-line gone, (b) Rumlow alive and contained, (c) a counter-introject of sufficient gravity to replace what was lost, (d) a *new ideological frame* he could absorb the way he absorbed the old one. The candidate frames are vanishingly few; an authoritarian temperament does not readily migrate to a non-authoritarian worldview, and an *anti*-authoritarian frame would not stick. The most plausible counter-introject would be something like a disciplined monastic or martial-religious order with hierarchy intact but cruelty proscribed — and even this is a long-shot graft.

- *Pathway 2: Slow erosion via lateral attachment.* Theoretically, a sustained non-coercive relationship — the thing his developmental history foreclosed — could, over years, generate a relational capacity that competes with the dominance-submission schema. The historical evidence suggests his only candidate for such a relationship is Diamondback, and the Diamondback record establishes that he cannot relate to her except through possession. There is no second candidate in the file. This pathway is essentially closed.

- *Pathway 3: A late-life depressive episode that finally penetrates the defenses and forces internal accounting.* Possible in principle. Would require the simultaneous removal of his external organizing supports (mission tempo, the Skull-line, Sin, the mask's social utility) and a physiological substrate (post-TBI depression is common; chronic-pain-mediated depression is common; he is at risk for both). Even granted the episode, the most likely outcome is suicide before reorganization, because his defenses are *outward* and despair would have nowhere to be discharged except inward.

The asymmetry is the honest finding. He has many roads to catastrophe and approximately one and a half to growth, and the growth roads require conditions the world is unlikely to assemble around him.

---

## 9.6 What an Adversary Should Plan For

The forward operational picture, condensed:

- **He will keep working until he physically cannot.** Plan for a fifteen-to-twenty-year continued threat horizon, not the ten that age tables would predict.
- **He will telegraph one large symbolic sortie before he is finished.** The intelligence task is to recognize the pre-sortie signature: increased personal involvement in target selection, return to first-person execution after a period of handler-only work, retrieval of personally meaningful weapons or operational signatures from the Gruenwald or Brubaker eras, a final farewell-coded interaction with Sin (or, if Sin is gone, with the Skull's iconography).
- **He will reproduce himself.** The pupil pipeline is the strategic threat; addressing Rumlow without addressing his cadre is short-sighted.
- **He is exploitable through the introject, not through the body.** Killing him solves a tactical problem and creates martyr-utility for the Skull-line. Corrupting his relationship to the Skull-line solves a strategic problem and creates either a paralyzed asset or a defector-asset of considerable value.
- **He is not redeemable on any timeline the operational environment will tolerate.** Plans premised on redemption — converting him, turning him, using him long-term as a reformed asset — will fail. Plans premised on temporary destabilization in the service of a specific operation can succeed if pursued with patience and informational sophistication.

---

## 9.7 The Final Projection in One Paragraph

He continues. He continues longer than the actuarial curve predicts because his pleasures do not age out and his identity has already absorbed the worst injury his body is likely to suffer. He continues to serve the Skull-line in whatever form it presents itself, with declining physical capacity offset by deepening tradecraft and rising symbolic ambition. He produces students, and the students are the durable threat. Somewhere in the next fifteen years he engineers a terminal sortie at a target whose symbolism justifies, in his frame, the expenditure of himself, and he dies executing it or in the immediate aftermath, the mask still on. Between now and then, the only event that could meaningfully alter this arc is the severance of his organizing object under conditions that prevent him from immediately substituting a new one — and even that produces, most likely, a faster and uglier version of the same ending rather than a different one. The dossier closes on a subject whose future is unusually legible precisely because his interior was, in the end, unusually simple: a structure built once, in adolescence, around a temperament built before that, and never meaningfully rebuilt. Forward assessment, accordingly, is not prediction so much as *extrapolation along a line that has not yet bent and gives no indication of bending.*

— END SECTION 9.
